2:22:1310:0:14:72:284:700:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:Estimating Matching Games with Transfers 
2:23:1350:14:14:71:141:686:12:Times:12:Times:Jeremy T. Fox
2:24:1363:14:14:71:236:672:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:NBER Working Paper No. 14382 
2:25:1391:14:14:71:243:658:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:October 2008, Revised March 2016
2:26:1423:14:28:71:242:644:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. C1,C14,C71,D85,L22,L62
2:27:1453:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:28:1461:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:I  explore  the  estimation  of  transferable  utility  matching  games,  encompassing  many-to-many 
2:29:1562:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:matching, marriage  and  matching  with  trading  networks  (trades).  I  introduce  a  matching 
2:30:1658:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:maximum  score  estimator that  does  not  suffer  from  a  computational  curse  of  dimensionality  in 
2:31:1762:14:14:71:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:the number of agents in a matching market. I apply the estimator to data on the car parts supplied 
2:32:1860:14:14:71:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:by automotive suppliers to estimate the returns from different portfolios of parts to suppliers and 
2:33:1959:14:42:71:184:518:12:Times:12:Times:automotive assemblers.
2:34:1981:42:14:71:141:476:12:Times:12:Times:Jeremy T. Fox
2:35:1994:14:14:71:147:462:12:Times:12:Times:Rice University
2:36:2009:14:14:71:236:448:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics - MS22
2:37:2039:14:14:71:123:434:12:Times:12:Times:Baker Hall
2:38:2049:14:14:71:142:420:12:Times:12:Times:P.O. Box 1892
2:39:2062:14:14:71:195:406:12:Times:12:Times:Houston, TX 77251-1892
2:40:2084:14:14:71:123:392:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
2:41:2092:14:0:71:182:378:12:Times:12:Times:jeremyfox@gmail.com
3:42:2111:0:25:86:196:695:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:1  Introduction
3:43:2126:25:15:86:525:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:There are many situations in which economists have data on relationships, including marriages between
3:44:2227:15:15:86:525:655:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:men and women and partnerships between upstream and downstream firms. Economists wish to use
3:45:2319:15:15:86:525:640:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the data on the set of realized relationships to estimate the valuations of agents over the characteristics
3:46:2426:15:14:86:525:625:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of potential partners and other measured aspects of the relationships.  This is a challenging task
3:47:2524:14:15:86:525:611:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:compared to estimating valuations using more traditional data because we observe only the equilibrium
3:48:2625:15:15:86:525:596:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:relationships and not each agent’s equilibrium choice set: the identity of the other agents who would
3:49:2726:15:15:86:525:581:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:be willing to match with a particular agent. We must infer utility parameters from the sorting seen
3:50:2825:15:15:86:137:566:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in the data.
3:51:2837:15:15:101:525:551:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:This paper presents an estimator for transferable utility matching games.  Transferable utility
3:52:2932:15:15:86:525:536:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:matching games feature prices (or transfers) for relationships. This paper primarily models the for-
3:53:3032:15:15:86:525:521:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:mation of relationships as a competitive equilibrium to the matching model of Azevedo and Hatfield
3:54:3130:15:15:86:525:506:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(2015, Section 6), which uses a continuum of agents. This model is quite general and includes many
3:55:3228:15:15:86:525:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:special cases of empirical interest.1Equilibrium existence and uniqueness are generically satisfied.
3:56:3328:15:15:86:525:476:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The paper briefly considers the related model of Hatfield, Kominers, Nichifor, Ostrovsky and West-
3:57:3426:15:15:86:525:461:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:kamp (2013), which uses a finite number of agents. In these models, a generalization of a match is
3:58:3524:15:15:86:525:446:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:called a trade. A trade can include other aspects in addition to the identity of the match partners.
3:59:3624:15:15:86:525:431:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:For example, in a labor market a trade could specify the number of hours an employee is to work per
3:60:3723:15:15:86:295:416:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:week and the number of vacation days per year.
3:61:3769:15:15:101:525:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Using this structure, the paper explores the estimation of valuation functions, which represent the
3:62:3868:15:15:86:525:386:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:structural preference of agents for matches or trades. Computational challenges are key in match-
3:63:3965:15:14:86:525:371:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:ing and a computationally simple matching maximum score estimator is introduced to address the
3:64:4059:14:15:86:525:357:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:computational challenges. In an application, the paper uses the matching maximum score estimator
3:65:4155:15:15:86:525:342:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:to empirically answer questions related to the car parts industry. I first describe the methodological
3:66:4257:15:15:86:296:327:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:contribution and then the empirical application.
3:67:4305:15:15:101:525:312:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Computational issues in matching games are paramount and, in my opinion, have limited the
3:68:4394:15:15:86:525:297:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:prior use of matching games in empirical work. Matching markets often have hundreds of agents in
3:69:4490:15:15:86:525:282:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:them, compared to, say, the two to five agents often modeled as potential entrants in applications of
3:70:4591:15:15:86:525:267:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Nash entry games in industrial organization. In the car parts data, there are 2627 car parts in one
3:71:4690:15:15:86:525:252:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:so-called car component category. In Fox and Bajari (2013), we apply the estimator introduced in
3:72:4786:15:15:86:525:237:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:this paper to the matching between bidders and items for sale in a FCC spectrum auction. There are
3:73:4884:15:15:86:525:222:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:85 winning bidders and 480 items for sale in the auction application. Both the car parts and auction
3:74:4984:15:15:86:525:207:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:datasets are rich. There is a lot of information on agent characteristics and unknown parameters that
3:75:5085:15:15:86:525:192:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:can be learned from the observed sorting of car part suppliers to car assemblers or bidders to items
3:76:5185:15:15:86:525:177:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for sale. To take advantage of rich data sets, a researcher must use an estimator that allows for the
3:77:5286:15:15:86:239:162:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:dimensionality of typical problems.
3:78:5321:15:15:101:525:147:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The solution in maximum score is to introduce inequalities that are computationally simple to
3:79:5414:15:14:86:525:132:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:work with. The objective function is proportional to the number of inequalities that are true at a
3:80:5512:14:13:97:525:118:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:1Some initial papers on one-to-one, two-sided matching with transferable utility are Koopmans and Beckmann (1957);
3:81:5626:13:9:86:525:105:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:Gale (1960); Shapley and Shubik (1972); Becker (1973). This paper uses the term “matching game” to encompass a
3:82:5736:9:10:86:525:96:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:broad class of transferable utility models, including some games where the original theoretical analyses used different
3:83:5855:10:0:86:111:86:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:names.
4:84:5862:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:value for the unknown parameters in the valuation function. The inequalities involve only observable
4:85:5962:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:characteristics of matches, trades and unknown parameters. While there are unobservables in the
4:86:6057:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:true matching model, the maximum score inequalities do not require numerically integrating out
4:87:6151:15:15:86:525:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:unobservables, as in simulation estimators (McFadden, 1989; Pakes and Pollard, 1989; Hajivassiliou
4:88:6249:15:15:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and McFadden, 1998).  Therefore, the estimator does not suffer from computational issues due to
4:89:6344:15:15:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:numerical integration. Further, the integrand of the integral in a simulation estimator for a game
4:90:6442:15:14:86:525:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:theoretic model often involves a nested fixed point procedure to compute an equilibrium to the game
4:91:6541:14:15:86:525:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(for each simulation draw). No nested fixed point procedure is used in maximum score. Finally, only
4:92:6640:15:15:86:525:576:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a subset of the valid inequalities in maximum score can be included without losing the estimator’s
4:93:6738:15:15:86:199:561:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(point or set) consistency.
4:94:6765:15:15:101:525:546:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The curse of dimensionality for other estimators can be seen for a simple, one-to-one matching
4:95:6859:15:15:86:525:531:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:market with 100 men and 100 women.  If no agents can be unmatched, for simplicity, there are
4:96:6951:15:15:86:525:516:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f4:1002= 10,000possible matches and100!≈10158possible assignments. If there are match-specific
4:97:7042:15:15:86:525:501:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:unobservables, the likelihood function involves a numerical integral of 10,000 dimensions and an in-
4:98:7142:15:15:86:526:486:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tegrand that involves computing whether 1 out of10158assignments occur. Of course, simulation
4:99:7235:15:15:86:525:471:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimators (sometimes based on moment conditions chosen for tractability) can be used for matching
4:100:7333:15:15:86:525:456:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:when required at least when markets are small and computational resources are large, as in Boyd,
4:101:7429:15:15:86:525:441:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Lankford, Loeb and Wyckoff (2013), Sørensen (2007), Agarwal and Diamond (2013) and Fox, Hsu
4:102:7520:15:15:86:161:426:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and Yang (2015).
4:103:7536:15:15:101:525:411:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The computational advantages of matching maximum score are also present in single agent, multi-
4:104:7631:15:15:86:525:396:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:nomial choice maximum score (Manski, 1975; Matzkin, 1993; Briesch, Chintagunta and Matzkin, 2002;
4:105:7728:15:15:86:525:381:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Fox, 2007). Indeed, this paper shows that, under some assumptions, a single agent maximum score
4:106:7823:15:15:86:525:366:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimator can be applied to matching data if the prices of matches or trades are observed in the data.
4:107:7925:15:15:86:525:351:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Akkus, Cookson and Hortacsu (forthcoming) and Fox and Bajari (2013, Section VI.B, Appendix C)
4:108:8018:15:14:86:525:336:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:apply single agent maximum score estimators to matching data with prices. However, in many ap-
4:109:8112:14:15:86:525:322:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:plications prices are not observed. For example, in marriage prices paid between men and women
4:110:8206:15:15:86:525:307:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:are rarely observed and prices are private contractual details in the car parts industry studied here.
4:111:8308:15:15:86:525:292:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Without price data, a contribution of this paper is to propose matching maximum score inequalities
4:112:8406:15:15:86:525:277:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:that do not use price data. The paper proves that the maximum score setup results at least in set
4:113:8503:15:15:86:525:262:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:identification under the Azevedo and Hatfield (2015, Section 6) model with a continuum of agents and
4:114:8603:15:15:86:168:247:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:other assumptions.
4:115:8621:15:15:101:525:232:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The use of a model with a continuum of agents as the true or limiting matching model dates to
4:116:8714:15:15:86:525:217:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the pioneering work on estimating matching games by Choo and Siow (2006). Choo and Siow studied
4:117:8809:15:15:86:525:202:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the case of one-to-one, two-sided matching or marriage. They assume that the unobservables have the
4:118:8908:15:15:86:525:187:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:type I extreme value distribution, resulting in a logit choice model at the agent level and closed form
4:119:9011:15:15:86:525:172:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:formulas for matching patterns.2Chiappori, Salanié and Weiss (2015) and Galichon and Salanie (2012)
4:120:9110:15:15:86:525:157:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:use the term separability to highlight a key assumption in Choo and Siow. Separability restricts how
4:121:9210:15:15:86:525:142:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:agents’ unobservable components of valuations vary across matches or trades. The main results of this
4:122:9311:15:12:97:525:127:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:2Dagsvik (2000) provides logit-based methods for studying matching games where other aspects of a relationship than
4:123:9426:12:9:86:525:115:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:money are also part of the pairwise stable matching. Although he does not emphasize it, one-to-one matching games
4:124:9539:9:10:86:525:106:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:with transferable utility are a special case of his analysis. Matching games with transfers are also related to models
4:125:9657:10:9:86:525:96:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:of hedonic equilibria, where estimators typically use data on the prices of trades (Rosen, 1974; Ekeland, Heckman and
4:126:9774:9:0:86:293:87:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:Nesheim, 2004; Heckman, Matzkin and Nesheim, 2010).
5:127:9826:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:paper also rely on separability and this assumption is discussed in some detail below. Separability fits
5:128:9930:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:well into the matching model of Azevedo and Hatfield (2015, Section 6). Previous versions of this paper
5:129:10033:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:introduced the matching maximum score estimator for many-to-many, two-sided matching and used
5:130:10126:15:15:86:525:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the closed form logit formulas from Choo and Siow to show the estimator’s consistency for the simpler
5:131:10227:15:15:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:marriage model. However, it was Graham (2011, Theorem 4.1) who, in a survey article discussing
5:132:10321:15:15:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:previous drafts of this paper, first proved set identification for the continuum marriage model under
5:133:10422:15:14:86:525:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:semiparametric conditions nearly identical to those used for proving set identification for single agent
5:134:10526:14:15:86:525:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:maximum score models (Manski, 1975; Matzkin, 1993; Briesch, Chintagunta and Matzkin, 2002; Fox,
5:135:10621:15:15:86:525:576:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:2007). The current version of this paper introduces the matching maximum score estimator, uses the
5:136:10719:15:15:86:525:561:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:setup of the quite general Azevedo and Hatfield (2015, Section 6) model and extends the argument of
5:137:10818:15:15:86:302:546:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Graham for marriage to the more general setting.
5:138:10866:15:15:101:525:531:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:This paper was originally part of a larger project including Fox (2007) on maximum score methods
5:139:10962:15:15:86:525:516:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for single agent multinomial choice, Fox (2010) on nonparametric identification in matching games,
5:140:11060:15:15:86:525:501:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and Fox and Bajari (2013) on an empirical application of the matching maximum score estimator to
5:141:11156:15:15:86:525:486:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:an FCC spectrum auction. Earlier working paper versions of this paper have circulated since 2005, at
5:142:11256:15:15:86:525:471:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the same time as drafts of these other papers. The methodological contribution of the current paper is
5:143:11358:15:15:86:525:456:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the introduction of the matching maximum score estimator and the discussion of its theoretical (set)
5:144:11458:15:15:86:525:441:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:consistency using the high generality of the matching model of Azevedo and Hatfield (2015, Section
5:145:11556:15:15:86:525:426:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:6). Earlier drafts of this paper focused on models of many-to-many, two-sided matching and special
5:146:11654:15:15:86:482:411:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:cases thereof (such as one-to-one matching). The empirical work on car parts is also novel.
5:147:11745:15:15:101:525:396:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The matching maximum score estimator has been used in empirical work in many published papers
5:148:11838:15:15:86:525:381:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and circulating working papers by now. Citing many of them would risk offending those omitted,
5:149:11932:15:15:86:525:366:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:but the breadth of applications to different fields of applied microeconomics and business shows the
5:150:12032:15:15:86:525:351:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:usefulness of the maximum score approach to matching estimation. Graham (2011) and Chiappori
5:151:12124:15:14:86:525:336:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and Salanié (forthcoming), both mostly for marriage, as well as Mindruta, Moeen and Agarwal (2015),
5:152:12223:14:15:86:525:322:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for the academic field of strategy, are three published surveys that extensively discuss the matching
5:153:12324:15:15:86:525:307:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:maximum score estimator. The Mindruta et al. survey is particularly useful for those wishing to
5:154:12419:15:15:86:525:292:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:compare a matching game theoretic approach to working with relationship data to other empirical
5:155:12514:15:15:86:525:277:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:approaches, such as so-called dyad regressions. I have made code for the matching maximum score
5:156:12609:15:15:86:283:262:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimator available (Santiago and Fox, 2009).
5:157:12654:15:15:101:525:247:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I cite some other methodological papers on matching in the rest of the text. One paper that is
5:158:12748:15:15:86:525:232:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:not cited below is Menzel (2015), who studies marriage and shows that a class of semiparametric
5:159:12843:15:15:86:525:217:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:non-transferable utility matching models (not considered here) converge, as the market grows large,
5:160:12942:15:15:86:525:202:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:to a parametric matching model with matching formulas quite similar to the matching formulas in
5:161:13037:15:15:86:525:187:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the logit transferable utility marriage matching model with a continuum of agents in Choo and Siow
5:162:13135:15:15:86:525:172:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(2006). The current paper consider the continuum matching model of Azevedo and Hatfield (2015,
5:163:13229:15:15:86:525:157:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Section 6) and the semiparametric assumptions are made in the continuum; in no sense is a parametric
5:164:13329:15:0:86:309:142:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:model used as an approximation to the continuum.
6:165:13378:0:21:86:325:695:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:1.1  Empirical Application to Car Parts
6:166:13417:21:15:86:525:674:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A car is one of the most complex goods that an individual consumer will purchase. Cars are made
6:167:13512:15:15:86:525:659:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:up of hundreds of parts and the performance of the supply chain is critical to the performance of
6:168:13609:15:15:86:525:644:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:automobile assemblers and the entire industry. This paper investigates two related questions that are
6:169:13710:15:15:86:525:629:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:relevant to policy debates on the car parts industry. The first question relates to the productivity
6:170:13810:15:15:86:525:614:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:loss to suppliers from breaking up large assemblers of cars. During a recent large recession, North
6:171:13909:15:15:86:525:599:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:American-based automobile assemblers went through financial distress.  As a consequence, North
6:172:14003:15:15:86:525:584:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:American-based assemblers divested or closed both North American brands (General Motor’s Saturn)
6:173:14099:15:15:86:525:569:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and European brands (Ford’s Volvo) and seriously considered the divestment of other brands (GM’s
6:174:14195:15:15:86:525:554:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:large European subsidiary Opel). One loss from divesting a brand is that future product development
6:175:14294:15:15:86:525:539:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:will no longer be coordinated across as many brands under one parent company. If GM were to divest
6:176:14392:15:15:86:525:524:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Opel, which was a serious policy debate in Germany in 2009, then any benefit from coordinating new
6:177:14490:15:15:86:525:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:products across Opel and GM’s North American operations would be lost. This is a loss to GM, but
6:178:14586:15:15:86:525:494:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:also to the suppliers of GM, who will no longer be able to gain as much from specializing in supplying
6:179:14688:15:14:86:507:479:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:GM. I estimate the valuations to suppliers and to assemblers for different portfolios of car parts.
6:180:14787:14:15:101:525:465:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The second question this paper investigates is the extent to which the presence of foreign and in
6:181:14884:15:15:86:525:450:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:particular Japanese and Korean (Asian) assemblers in North America improves the North American
6:182:14978:15:15:86:525:435:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:supplier base. There is a general perception, backed by studies that I cite, that Asian automobile
6:183:15076:15:15:86:525:420:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:assemblers produce cars of higher quality. Part of producing a car of higher quality is sourcing car
6:184:15176:15:15:86:525:405:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:parts of higher quality. Therefore, Asian assemblers located in North America might improve North
6:185:15273:15:15:86:525:390:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:American suppliers’ qualities.  Understanding the role of foreign entrants on the North American
6:186:15369:15:15:86:525:375:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:supplier base is important for debates about trade barriers that encourage Asian assemblers to locate
6:187:15470:15:15:86:525:360:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:plants in North America in order to avoid those barriers. Trade barriers might indirectly benefit North
6:188:15573:15:15:86:525:345:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:American assemblers by encouraging higher quality North American suppliers to operate in order to
6:189:15670:15:15:86:525:330:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:supply Asian-owned assembly plants in North America. I place this investigation in an appendix as
6:190:15767:15:15:86:296:315:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the key parameter has a wide confidence region.
6:191:15814:15:15:101:525:300:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I answer both of the above questions using the identities of the companies that supply each car
6:192:15909:15:15:86:525:285:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:part. The data list each car model and each car part on that model, and importantly the supplier of
6:193:16008:15:15:86:525:270:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:each car part. The intuition is that the portfolio of car parts that each supplier manufactures informs
6:194:16111:15:15:86:525:255:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:us about the factors that make a successful supplier.  If each supplier sells car parts to only two
6:195:16210:15:15:86:525:240:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:assemblers, it may be that suppliers benefit from specialization at the assembly firm level. If North
6:196:16311:15:15:86:525:225:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:American suppliers to Asian-owned assemblers are also likely to supply parts to North American-
6:197:16406:15:14:86:462:210:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:owned assemblers, it may be because of a quality advantage that those suppliers have.
6:198:16491:14:15:101:525:196:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:This paper takes the stand that the sorting pattern of sellers (suppliers like Bosch and Delphi) to
6:199:16590:15:15:86:525:181:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:buyers (assemblers like General Motors and Toyota) informs us about so-called valuation functions,
6:200:16688:15:15:86:525:166:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:key components of total profits, generating the payoffs of particular portfolios of car part trades to
6:201:16790:15:15:86:525:151:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:assemblers and to suppliers. In turn, the valuation functions for assemblers and suppliers help us
6:202:16888:15:15:86:525:136:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:answer the policy questions about government-induced divestitures and foreign assembler plants in
6:203:16985:15:15:86:525:121:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:North America. The loss to a supplier from GM divesting Opel occurs when supplying two car parts
6:204:17081:15:15:86:525:106:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:to a large parent company generates more valuation than supplying one car part each to two different
6:205:17181:15:0:86:525:91:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:assemblers. Thus, the valuation of a portfolio of trades is not necessarily the sum of the valuations
7:206:17283:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:from individual trades.  The portfolio of trades of each firm is critical for valuations.  Therefore,
7:207:17384:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:valuation functions are not additively separable across multiple trades, as they are in most prior work
7:208:17487:15:15:86:450:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:on matching not employing the maximum score estimator introduced in this paper.
7:209:17566:15:15:101:525:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I model the market for car parts as a two-sided, many-to-many matching game, with the two
7:210:17655:15:15:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:sides being assemblers and suppliers. In a competitive equilibrium, each firm will form the trades, car
7:211:17758:15:15:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:part transactions, that maximize its profits at the market-clearing prices. However, those prices are
7:212:17859:15:14:86:525:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:confidential contractual details not released to researchers. This motivates the use of the matching
7:213:17959:14:38:86:267:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:maximum score estimator without prices.
7:214:17998:38:22:86:525:553:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2  Example 1: Matching Maximum Score Estimator for Mar-
7:215:18053:22:25:110:144:531:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:riage
7:216:18058:25:15:86:525:506:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I first introduce the matching maximum score estimator for the simple case of one-to-one, two-sided
7:217:18157:15:15:86:525:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:matching, which I label Example 1. While many examples fit a one-to-one, two-sided matching setup,
7:218:18255:15:15:86:525:476:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the case getting the most attention in the structural empirical literature is heterosexual, monoga-
7:219:18354:15:15:86:525:461:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:mous marriage. In order to communicate the implementation of the proposed method to empirical
7:220:18447:15:15:86:525:446:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:researchers, this section discusses only the estimator that a researcher codes on the computer and does
7:221:18550:15:15:86:525:431:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:not cover many underlying modeling details, such as unobservable terms. These modeling details are
7:222:18648:15:15:86:190:416:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:introduced in Section 3.
7:223:18672:15:15:101:525:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The researcher has data on ̃Nmarriages. View these as a random sample of the marriages from
7:224:18763:15:15:86:525:386:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a larger market. For each marriage, the researcher observes some characteristics of the malejmand
7:225:18860:15:15:86:525:371:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f14:some characteristics of the femalejf.  The researcher uses these characteristics to specify ajoint
7:226:18958:15:15:86:525:356:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f4:valuation function based on observable types ̃X(jm,jf)′θ, which is specified to be equal to a
7:227:19051:15:14:86:525:341:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f8:finite vector of observables ̃X(jm,jf)times a vector of unknown parametersθ. The vector ̃X(jm,jf)
7:228:19148:14:15:86:525:327:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:is chosen by the researcher based on the available data on agent characteristics. The choice of the
7:229:19247:15:15:86:525:312:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:elements of ̃X(jm,jf)ideally should be informed by results on the nonparametric identification of
7:230:19344:15:15:86:525:297:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:joint valuation functions in matching games, such as the discussion of Becker (1973) and Fox (2010)
7:231:19443:15:15:86:526:282:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:below. Note that the researcher can construct the vector ̃X(jm,jf)for a marriage that did not form
7:232:19541:15:15:86:420:267:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in the data by varying the observable characteristics of the male and female.
7:233:19618:15:15:101:525:252:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The underlying transferable utility matching model follows Becker (1973) and the large subsequent
7:234:19715:15:15:86:525:237:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:literature and uses prices for marriage. Men pay women possibly negative transfers. However, consis-
7:235:19815:15:15:86:525:222:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tent with actual data and previous structural empirical work on transferable utility matching models
7:236:19915:15:15:86:525:207:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of marriage, prices are assumed not to be in the available data (Choo and Siow, 2006). Maximum
7:237:20009:15:15:86:311:192:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:score estimation with price data is discussed below.
7:238:20061:15:15:101:525:177:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Letiindex the male in a marriage and letf(i)index the female married to him in equilibrium.
7:239:20152:15:15:86:525:162:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Sojimis the characteristics of maleiandjf(i)fis the characteristics of femalef(i). A competitive
7:240:20248:15:15:86:525:147:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:equilibrium (equivalent in this model to a stable matching) to this transferable utility matching game
7:241:20350:15:15:86:525:132:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:isefficient: it maximizes the sum of joint valuations across all marriages in the entire economy. If
7:242:20450:15:15:86:525:117:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:there were no unobservables (and recall that there are in the true model), an implication of social
7:243:20549:15:0:86:525:102:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:efficiency is that swapping spouses lowers the sum of joint valuations. Therefore, intuition suggests
8:244:20651:0:25:86:465:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the followingmatching maximum score inequalityshould be useful in estimation:
8:245:20728:25:0:146:151:670:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f10: ̃X
8:246:20731:0:11:154:160:679:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
8:247:20732:11:0:160:184:668:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f13:ji1m,jf(i1)f
8:248:20744:0:11:199:207:679:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f15:)′
8:249:20746:11:0:209:234:668:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:θ+ ̃X
8:250:20751:0:11:237:243:679:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
8:251:20752:11:0:243:267:668:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f13:ji2m,jf(i2)f
8:252:20764:0:11:282:290:679:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f15:)′
8:253:20766:11:0:293:319:668:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:θ≥ ̃X
8:254:20771:0:11:321:327:679:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
8:255:20772:11:0:327:352:668:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f13:ji1m,jf(i2)f
8:256:20784:0:11:366:374:679:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f15:)′
8:257:20786:11:0:377:402:668:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:θ+ ̃X
8:258:20791:0:11:405:411:679:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
8:259:20792:11:0:411:435:668:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f13:ji2m,jf(i1)f
8:260:20804:0:11:450:458:679:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f15:)′
8:261:20806:11:28:460:525:668:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:θ.(1)
8:262:20811:28:15:86:525:640:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The inequality says that the sum of joint valuations of two observed matches should weakly exceed
8:263:20908:15:15:86:525:625:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the sum of the joint valuations from the two matches where the married couples exchange spouses:
8:264:21004:15:14:86:525:610:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:malei1is married to femalef(i2)instead of his actual wifef(i1), for example. If single people are in
8:265:21104:14:15:86:525:596:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the data, one can normalize the valuation from being single to 0, add a constant term toX(jm,jf),
8:266:21201:15:15:86:525:581:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and include being single as a “spouse” for males and females in matching maximum score inequalities.
8:267:21301:15:15:86:525:566:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Using data on singles would slightly complicate the notation for the summations below. Note that the
8:268:21401:15:15:86:525:551:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:competitive equilibrium being efficient is used for intuition for motivating matching maximum score
8:269:21500:15:15:86:525:536:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:inequalities in the main text. However, the formal proofs in the appendix do not rely on a competitive
8:270:21602:15:15:86:202:521:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:equilibrium being efficient.
8:271:21630:15:21:101:354:506:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Thematching maximum score objective functionis

8:296:21779:14:35:493:525:471:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:.(2)
8:297:21783:35:15:86:525:436:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The dependent variable here is the matches in the data,f(i)for mani. The matching maximum score,
8:298:21879:15:15:86:525:421:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:or maximum rank correlation as explained below, objective function checks whether each matching
8:299:21974:15:15:86:525:406:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:maximum score inequality is true.  If an inequality is true for a guess of the parameter vectorθ,
8:300:22071:15:15:86:525:391:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the objective function increases by 1. Not all inequalities will be true even at the true value of the
8:301:22173:15:15:86:525:376:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:parameter vectorθbecause of unobservable variables present in the model, as introduced below.
8:302:22266:15:15:86:525:361:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The objective function is a step function. The code in Santiago and Fox (2009) uses the differential
8:303:22366:15:15:86:525:346:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:evolution global optimization routine; other choices are possible. If the parameterθin the maximum
8:304:22464:15:15:86:525:331:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:score model is point identified (as discussed below), any maximizer of the objective function is a
8:305:22562:15:15:86:525:316:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:consistent estimator.  If the underlying parameterθin the model is instead set identified, then a
8:306:22659:15:15:86:525:301:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:valid 95% confidence set for the identified parameters should be reported. Note that point and set
8:307:22757:15:14:86:525:286:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:identification as used here are properties of the probability limit (expectation) of the objective function,
8:308:22865:14:15:86:525:272:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:not the objective function for a finite sample of data. More discussion of inference and point vs set
8:309:22966:15:15:86:184:257:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:identification is below.
8:310:22990:15:15:101:525:242:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The matching maximum score objective function is easy to compute: it involves only addition,
8:311:23082:15:15:86:525:227:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:multiplication and checking an inequality. There is no numerical integration over unobservables and
8:312:23181:15:15:86:525:212:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:no nested fixed point computation of equilibria. There is no attempt to estimate a distribution of
8:313:23279:15:15:86:525:197:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:unobservables using sieve methods or to estimate matching probabilities nonparametrically in a first
8:314:23379:15:15:86:525:182:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:stage. Further, the objective function is written as if all possible inequalities will be used. But the
8:315:23482:15:15:86:525:167:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:available inequalities can be randomly sampled and the estimator will still be consistent. Altogether,
8:316:23584:15:15:86:525:152:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I can say that the estimator does not suffer from a computational or data curse of dimensionality in
8:317:23684:15:15:86:332:137:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the size of the data on the matching market in question.
8:318:23740:15:15:101:526:122:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:If the researcher has data onDindependent matching markets (say different towns in the marriage
8:319:23835:15:0:86:525:107:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:example), then the researcher merely adds an extra summation (and market indicesd) to the objective
9:320:23935:0:21:86:122:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:function

9:349:24065:15:14:86:525:624:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Asymptotics could be in the number of marketsDor, for fixedD, some notion ̃Nof the number of
9:350:24157:14:15:86:525:610:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:recorded marriages such that each ̃Nd=νd· ̃Nfor the fixed-with- ̃Nmarket-specific proportionality
9:351:24254:15:38:86:217:595:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:factorsνd, as discussed below.
9:352:24284:38:25:86:221:557:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3  Matching Game
9:353:24300:25:15:86:525:532:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Matching games model relationship formation. This paper discusses estimation of the transferable
9:354:24396:15:15:86:525:517:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:utility matching game with a continuum of agents in Azevedo and Hatfield (2015, Section 6), hence-
9:355:24494:15:14:86:525:502:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:forth abbreviated as the AH model. An otherwise similar model with a finite number of agents in is
9:356:24592:14:15:86:525:488:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Hatfield, Kominers, Nichifor, Ostrovsky and Westkamp (2013). Valuations in the AH model encom-
9:357:24686:15:15:86:525:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:pass valuations for a great many applications of empirical interest, including the previous example of
9:358:24788:15:15:86:525:458:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:marriage and many-to-many, two-sided matching with valuations defined over sets of matches. This
9:359:24884:15:15:86:525:443:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:generality is useful for scholars applying the matching maximum score estimator to matching games
9:360:24981:15:15:86:525:428:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:other than marriage and the one estimated for the car parts industry later in this paper. I discuss
9:361:25080:15:15:86:525:413:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:several special cases of the AH model below.  The AH model has desirable properties: a unique
9:362:25173:15:15:86:410:398:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:competitive equilibrium exists under fairly innocuous technical conditions.
9:363:25248:15:15:101:525:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The arguments in this section lead to an estimation approach that uses data on one large matching
9:364:25345:15:15:86:525:368:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:market, as considered previously for one-to-one matching by Choo and Siow (2006) and the related
9:365:25441:15:15:86:525:353:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:work cited in the introduction. The asymptotic argument increases the sample size as the number
9:366:25536:15:15:86:525:338:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of agents observed in the data grow large. In an early application, Fox and Bajari (2013) use the
9:367:25633:15:15:86:525:323:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:matching maximum score estimator and the large market asymptotic argument to study a large
9:368:25723:15:15:86:164:308:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:spectrum auction.
9:369:25740:15:15:101:525:293:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:In the large market asymptotic argument, the limiting matching game, here the AH model, has
9:370:25831:15:15:86:525:278:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a continuum of agents. AH show that there exists a unique equilibrium to this matching game. The
9:371:25927:15:15:86:525:263:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:equilibrium is deterministic in the aggregate. As a researcher collects more data, the asymptotic fiction
9:372:26032:15:15:86:525:248:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:is that the researcher is observing more agents from this limiting game. Therefore, the asymptotic
9:373:26130:15:14:86:525:233:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:fiction of collecting more data does not alter the outcome of the matching game in question; the
9:374:26226:14:32:86:473:219:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:researcher is merely learning more about an existing market with a continuum of agents.
9:375:26313:32:21:86:206:187:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:3.1  The AH Model

10:461:28831:7:12:97:525:114:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:4AH require two further technical conditions. Using their words and skipping their notation: 1) The integral of
10:462:28942:12:10:86:525:102:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:absolute values of utility is finite as long as agents are not given bundles for which they have utility of−∞and 2)
10:463:29057:10:0:86:320:92:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:agents can supply any sufficiently small net demand for trades.
11:464:29121:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:sense then the price vectorpΩin the competitive equilibrium is unique. Given these relatively weak
11:465:29219:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:conditions for equilibrium existence and uniqueness, I maintain existence and uniqueness in what
11:466:29315:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:follows. What actually matters for the empirical approach is that the same competitive equilibrium
11:467:29413:15:31:86:324:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:is being played by all agents in the continuum market.
11:468:29467:31:21:86:331:619:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:3.2  Observable and Unobservable Types
11:469:29505:21:15:86:525:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The AH model has complete information in the sense that no attributes of a trade are privately
11:470:29599:15:15:86:525:583:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:observed.  Still, econometricians wish to distinguish between attributes of agents measured in the
11:471:29697:15:15:86:526:568:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:data and attributes not measured in the data. Recalliindexes a full agent type in the AH model.
11:472:29792:15:15:86:526:553:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Letjindex anobservable agent typein afiniteset of observable agent typesJand letkindex
11:473:29878:15:15:86:525:538:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:anunobservable agent typein some, likely infinite, setK, so that each full agent typeiuniquely
11:474:29972:15:15:86:525:523:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:corresponds to a pair of agent types(j,k). This focus on observables and unobservable (in data) agent
11:475:30073:15:15:86:446:508:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:types specializes the AH model but does not alter its properties mentioned before.
11:476:30155:15:15:101:525:493:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The set of tradesΩis finite in the AH model and here the set of observable agent typesJis also
11:477:30249:15:15:86:525:478:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:finite. Assume that the definition of a tradeωencodes the observable agent typeb(ω)∈Jfor the
11:478:30341:15:15:86:525:463:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:buyer on tradeωand the observable agent types(ω)∈Jfor the seller on tradeω. In the AH model,
11:479:30433:15:15:86:525:448:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:agents have preferences defined over trades. So an agenti∈Iis allowed to have preferences over the
11:480:30531:15:15:86:525:433:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:observable agent typesj∈Jof the counterparties to tradesω. In some examples of the AH model
11:481:30622:15:15:86:525:418:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:below, a tradeωencodesonlythe observable agent types of the buyerb(ω)and sellers(ω). Trades
11:482:30713:15:15:86:307:403:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:may encode other aspects, as also discussed below.
11:483:30763:15:15:101:525:388:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Tradesωdo not encode unobservable typesk. So agents are not allowed to have preferences over
11:484:30855:15:15:86:525:373:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the unobservable typesk∈Kof counterparties on tradesω. The set of unobservable (in data) agent
11:485:30949:15:14:86:525:358:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:typesKis not required to be finite. Indeed, a finite set of observable agent typesJand an uncountably
11:486:31050:14:15:86:525:344:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:infinite set of unobservable agent typesKin a model with a continuum of agents was first used in a
11:487:31148:15:15:86:525:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:parametric empirical model for one-to-one, two-sided matching (specifically, marriage) by Choo and
11:488:31246:15:15:86:525:314:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Siow (2006). Later for one-to-one, two-sided matching, Galichon and Salanie (2012) and Chiappori,
11:489:31343:15:15:86:525:299:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Salanié and Weiss (2015) used the term “separability” for the implementation in Choo and Siow of
11:490:31439:15:15:86:525:284:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:this sort of distinction between the cardinalities of observable and unobservable agent types. Like the
11:491:31542:15:15:86:525:269:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:marriage literature on models with a continuum of agents, I will maintain separability in part to use
11:492:31643:15:15:86:236:254:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the AH model’s greater generality.
11:493:31677:15:15:101:525:239:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f4:Separabilityin the AH model is defined as follows. Let the valuation of an agent of full type
11:494:31770:15:27:86:415:224:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:i∈Icorresponding to observable and unobservable types(j,k)∈J×Kbe
11:495:31834:27:28:244:367:197:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:vi(Φ,Ψ) =πj(Φ,Ψ) +-kΦ,Ψ,
11:496:31858:28:15:86:524:169:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f9:whereπjis thevaluation function for observable agent typejover trades(Φ,Ψ)and-kΦ,Ψ
11:497:31940:15:15:86:526:154:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:is theunobservable valuation componentfor unobservable agent typekand the set of trades
11:498:32027:15:15:86:526:139:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f4:(Φ,Ψ). Under separability,πjis a function of only the observable agent typejand the sets of trades
11:499:32125:15:15:86:525:124:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f4:ΦandΨ. All aspects of a tradeωare in the data, including the observable agent types of the buyer
11:500:32221:15:15:86:525:109:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:b(ω)∈Jand sellers(ω)∈J.5An agent of full typeialso has an unobservable valuation component
11:501:32311:15:0:97:390:94:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:5Letπj(Φ,Ψ) =−∞ifjis notb(ω)for anyω∈Φor nots(ω)for anyω∈Ψ.
12:502:32372:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:over the tradesΦandΨ, given by-kΦ,Ψ. The unobservable valuation components are separate for each
12:503:32468:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:set(Φ,Ψ)and so vary forkbased on the observable agent typesb(ω)ands(ω)of the agents on the
12:504:32558:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:other side of trades in(Φ,Ψ). However,-kΦ,Ψdoes not depend on the unobservable agent types for
12:505:32652:15:15:86:254:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the counterparties on trades in(Φ,Ψ).
12:506:32689:15:15:101:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Recall the distributionη(i)over agent full agent typesi∈I. Each full agent typeiis also the
12:507:32780:15:15:86:526:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:realization of an observable typejand the realization of an unobservable typekthat itself indexes
12:508:32877:15:0:86:224:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f8:a realization of the vector-k=
12:509:32907:0:9:228:233:614:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
12:510:32908:9:0:232:250:605:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f9:-kΦ,Ψ
12:511:32913:0:13:251:256:614:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
12:512:32914:13:0:255:358:601:7:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f10:Φ⊆Ω,Ψ⊆Ψ. The vector-
12:513:32934:0:18:358:525:609:7:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f4:kis of finite length because the set of
12:514:32973:18:0:86:403:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:tradesΩis finite.6Therefore,η(i)induces a joint distribution (CDF)F
12:515:33040:0:8:407:412:599:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
12:516:33041:8:0:412:433:591:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:-k|j
12:517:33045:0:8:433:438:599:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
12:518:33046:8:15:442:525:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for each observable
12:519:33065:15:15:86:525:576:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:agent typej.7By this notation, the vector-kis independently distributed across agents, conditional
12:520:33163:15:32:86:218:561:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:on the observable typesj∈J.
12:521:33190:32:21:86:173:529:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:3.3  Examples
12:522:33203:21:15:86:525:508:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f4:Example 1.Consider the monogamous, heterosexual marriage setting in Choo and Siow (2006),
12:523:33292:15:15:86:525:493:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Galichon and Salanie (2012) and Chiappori, Salanié and Weiss (2015), which uses separability and a
12:524:33390:15:15:86:525:478:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:continuum of agents. This is an example of one-to-one, two-sided matching.8The matching maximum
12:525:33485:15:15:86:525:463:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:score estimator was already previewed for this example in Section 2. Divide agents into males and
12:526:33582:15:15:86:525:448:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:females. Each observable agent typejcorresponds to a sex (male or female) and other observable
12:527:33676:15:15:86:525:433:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:demographic characteristics, such as age and race. Age is measured in integer years to have finite
12:528:33774:15:15:86:525:418:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:support.  A tradeωcorresponds to a marriage: a male observable typejm=b(ω)and a female
12:529:33860:15:15:86:525:403:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:observable typejf=s(ω). The pricepωof a trade is exchanged between males and females. Define
12:530:33952:15:15:86:525:388:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:πj(Φ,Ψ)to be−∞if any agent is engaged in more than one marriage or married to an agent of the
12:531:34045:15:15:86:525:373:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:same sex. Therefore, valuations for a male typeior(j,k)from matching with a female observable
12:532:34138:15:14:86:208:358:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:typejf=s(ω)specialize to
12:533:34162:14:23:277:334:344:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:πj(jf) +-kjf,
12:534:34175:23:15:86:525:321:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:whereπj(jf)is the valuation function for males with observable demographics injmatching to
12:535:34265:15:15:86:525:306:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:females with observable demographicsjfand-kjfis the preference of a male of unobservable typek
12:536:34359:15:15:86:525:291:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for females with demographic characteristicsjf. A symmetric valuation exists for females of typei.
12:537:34457:15:15:86:525:276:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Separability in the marriage setting means that males have preferences over female demographics, not
12:538:34557:15:15:86:525:261:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the unobservable type of the female they match with. While not considered in the cited empirical
12:539:34653:15:15:86:525:246:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:literature, it is straightforward to include aspects other than demographics into a tradeω. For example,
12:540:34757:15:15:86:525:231:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a tradeωcould specify the number of children or the hours of work of each spouse in a marriage.
12:541:34852:15:27:86:388:216:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Then the valuation for a male of typeior(j,k)for tradeωwould be
12:542:34915:27:16:280:331:189:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:πj(ω) +-kω.
12:543:34926:16:12:97:525:173:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:6The notation-kmeans the unique realization of the vector of unobservables corresponding to the unobservable
12:544:35034:12:7:86:300:161:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:agent typek. Whenkis a random variable, then so is-k.
12:545:35087:7:10:97:442:154:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:7One can safely drop the-kΦ,Ψfor a particularjand(Φ,Ψ)whenπj(Φ,Ψ) =−∞for thatj.
12:546:35166:10:13:97:525:144:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:8The two-sidedness (heterosexual marriage) defines Example 1 and is used in the cited empirical literature. The AH
12:547:35280:13:9:86:525:131:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:model can also be specialized to one-sided models of marriage: homosexual marriage or a model with both heterosexual
12:548:35396:9:0:86:183:122:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:and homosexual marriage.
13:549:35422:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A similar valuation exists for females. Empirical implementation of the more general notion of a trade
13:550:35524:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:requires the extra elements to be observable in the data, as in data on labor supply and the number
13:551:35623:15:43:86:318:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of children for each marriage that occurs in the data.
13:552:35677:43:15:86:525:622:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f4:Example 2.Say an agent is defined to be either a buyer or a seller ex ante, as in the empirical work
13:553:35777:15:15:86:525:607:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:on the car parts industry later in this paper. Then this is an example of two-sided, many-to-many
13:554:35874:15:15:86:525:592:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:matching. Defineπj(Φ,Ψ)to be−∞if an agent whose observable typej∈Jcorresponds to a buyer
13:555:35962:15:15:86:525:577:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:conducts trades as a seller, and similarly for a seller type. A tradeωspecifies the buyer observable
13:556:36062:15:15:86:525:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:typeb(ω)and the seller observable types(ω)in addition to possible other attributes, such as the
13:557:36157:15:15:86:525:547:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:quantity and quality of goods to deliver (if quantity and quality are specified on a finite grid and
13:558:36257:15:15:86:525:532:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:observable in the data for actual matches). Under separability, a buyer of full typeior(j,k)then has
13:559:36357:15:15:86:125:517:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:profits of
13:560:36367:15:0:259:318:502:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:πj(Φ) +-kΦ−
13:561:36378:0:22:321:335:512:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:∑
13:562:36379:22:0:320:337:490:7:g_d0_f13:7:g_d0_f9:ω∈Φ
13:563:36382:0:30:338:352:502:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:pω.
13:564:36385:30:15:86:525:472:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:As in marriage, the buyer’s unobservable valuation component-kΦdepends on the trades and hence on
13:565:36482:15:15:86:526:457:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the observable typess(ω)∈Jof the seller partners. Similarly, a seller full typeior(j,k)has profits
13:566:36580:15:15:86:94:442:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of
13:567:36582:15:0:258:319:427:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:πj(Ψ) +-kΨ+
13:568:36593:0:22:322:336:437:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:∑
13:569:36594:22:0:321:337:415:7:g_d0_f13:7:g_d0_f9:ω∈Ψ
13:570:36597:0:29:339:353:427:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:pω.
13:571:36600:29:15:86:525:398:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Recall that AH prove that a competitive equilibrium exists in this setting without ruling out em-
13:572:36697:15:15:86:525:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:pirically relevant cases, such as a functionπj(Φ)exhibiting complementarities across multiple trades
13:573:36797:15:15:86:525:368:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:involving the same agent. Complementarities across multiple trades involving the same agent are vital
13:574:36898:15:14:86:320:353:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:to the empirical application to the car parts industry.
13:575:36953:14:15:101:525:339:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The AH model requires that an agent’s valuation is directly a function of only the trades where
13:576:37048:15:15:86:525:324:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:that particular agent is a buyer or a seller. The AH model assumes awayexternalities: valuations
13:577:37144:15:15:86:525:309:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:defined over trades to which the agent does not participate. Competition for trades certainly affects
13:578:37245:15:15:86:526:294:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the price vector for trades,pΩ, although such competition for trades is not a valuation defined over
13:579:37345:15:15:86:525:279:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:trades to which the agent does not participate. True externalities could be important in applications;
13:580:37447:15:15:86:525:264:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for example if buyers are retailers and sellers are wholesalers and buyers compete with each other
13:581:37545:15:15:86:525:249:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for retail customers (outside of the matching game) after matching to sellers. Baccara, Imrohoroglu,
13:582:37645:15:15:86:525:234:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Wilson and Yariv (2012) use the matching maximum score estimator introduced in this paper to
13:583:37737:15:43:86:282:219:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimate a matching game with externalities.
13:584:37781:43:15:86:525:176:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f4:Example 3.Consider mergers between agents. An agent is not restricted to be a buyer or a seller
13:585:37876:15:15:86:525:161:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:ex ante.  If an agent acquires other agents in equilibrium, it ends up conducting only trades as a
13:586:37974:15:15:86:525:146:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:buyer although this is not specified ex ante. Likewise, an agent acquired by another agent ends up
13:587:38072:15:15:86:525:131:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:conducting only a single trade as a seller (if partial acquisitions are not modeled). Therefore, mergers
13:588:38176:15:15:86:525:116:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:are an example of one-sided matching, also called coalition formation.  If desired, one can define
13:589:38274:15:15:86:525:101:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:πj(Φ,Ψ)to be−∞if an agent of typejconducts trades as both a buyer and a seller or if an agent
13:590:38367:15:0:86:525:86:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:conducts two or more trades as a seller (target). The pricepωof a tradeωcaptures the price the
14:591:38463:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:buyer (acquirer) pays the seller (target). A tradeωspecifies the buyer observable agent typeb(ω)∈J
14:592:38561:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and the seller (target) observable agent types(ω)∈J. As in Uetake and Watanabe (2012), a trade
14:593:38655:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:may also specify other observable attributes, such as the equity split of the post-merger firm or the
14:594:38756:15:15:86:525:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:awarding of board seats to representatives of the acquirer and target. Akkus, Cookson and Hortacsu
14:595:38854:15:15:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(forthcoming) use a variant of the matching maximum score estimator with data on the prices of
14:596:38948:15:15:86:308:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tradespωto estimate a matching game of mergers.
14:597:38995:15:14:101:525:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:As mentioned above, the AH model does not incorporate externalities such as changes in the post-
14:598:39091:14:15:86:525:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:merger competition for customers between firms in the same industry. Therefore, the AH model is a
14:599:39188:15:46:86:461:576:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:better model of mergers when focusing on, say, across-industry conglomerate mergers.
14:600:39272:46:15:86:525:530:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f4:Example 4.Hatfield et al. (2013) mention the example of trading between dealers of used cars.
14:601:39365:15:15:86:525:515:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:There is a lively secondhand market in used cars. Dealers may both buy and sell used cars to other
14:602:39463:15:15:86:525:500:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:dealers. Here a tradeωspecifies the observable attributes of the used car in question and buyer and
14:603:39562:15:15:86:525:485:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:seller observable characteristicsb(ω),s(ω)∈J, including the dealer locations. A buyer might have
14:604:39658:15:15:86:525:470:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:valuations defined over the location of a seller in order to minimize transportation costs.  Dealers
14:605:39758:15:15:86:525:455:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:might have complex preferences over the set of used cars on their lot. For example, valuations might
14:606:39858:15:15:86:525:440:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:be higher from ending up with cars of only a certain brand or from having a diverse set of cars. The
14:607:39958:15:15:86:525:425:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:AH model does not restrict the valuations of dealers over the set of observable trades they undertake.
14:608:40060:15:15:86:525:410:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The set of cars that a dealer is endowed with (and possibly does not trade) can be included in the
14:609:40158:15:37:86:210:395:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:observable agent typej∈J.
14:610:40183:37:25:86:312:358:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:4  Identification and Estimation
14:611:40215:25:15:86:525:333:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:For expositional purposes, I first explore identification and estimation when data on the prices of
14:612:40314:15:15:86:525:318:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tradespΩare available. This discussion introduces concepts from the literature on single-agent choice
14:613:40415:15:15:86:525:303:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and applies them here, although the mathematical results on single-agent choice are not novel. The
14:614:40513:15:15:86:525:288:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:main purpose of this paper is to study identification and estimation for the case where data on the
14:615:40612:15:15:86:526:273:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:prices of tradespΩarenotavailable. The majority of this section discusses the matching maximum
14:616:40706:15:15:86:525:258:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:score estimator that does not use data on the prices of trades. This estimator was already introduced
14:617:40807:15:31:86:265:243:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for the example of marriage in Section 2.

16:739:45293:15:15:86:525:512:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f4:(Φ,Ψ). In the AH model, the set of tradesΩis finite so that there is no story in the model where any

16:758:46224:0:0:276:297:343:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:pω+
16:759:46227:0:22:302:316:353:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:∑
16:760:46228:22:0:299:319:331:7:g_d0_f13:5:g_d0_f18:ω∈Ψi
16:761:46232:0:0:321:414:343:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:pω≥X(ji,Φ,Ψ)′θ−
16:762:46247:0:22:417:431:353:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:∑
16:763:46248:22:0:416:433:331:7:g_d0_f13:7:g_d0_f9:ω∈Φ
16:764:46251:0:0:434:455:343:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:pω+
16:765:46254:0:22:458:472:353:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:∑
16:766:46255:22:0:457:473:331:7:g_d0_f13:7:g_d0_f9:ω∈Ψ
16:767:46258:0:0:475:485:343:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f13:pω
16:768:46260:0:17:486:492:360:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:]
16:769:46261:17:38:493:525:343:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:.(8)
16:770:46265:38:15:86:526:305:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The estimatorˆθNis any vector that maximizes the objective function. The maximum score objective
16:771:46361:15:15:86:525:290:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:function using price data is a step function and so a continuum of parameter values will maximize it;
16:772:46462:15:15:86:525:275:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:any rule to pick one (such as letting a numerical optimization routine decide) leads to a consistent
16:773:46562:15:15:86:525:260:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimator under point identification. Manski (1975) and Fox (2007) demonstrate the consistency of
16:774:46659:15:15:86:525:245:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the single agent estimator asN→∞. For the point identified case, Kim and Pollard (1990) present
16:775:46754:15:14:86:525:230:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the asymptotic distribution and Delgado, Rodriguez-Poo and Wolf (2001) discuss subsampling for
16:776:46848:14:15:86:525:216:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:straightforward inference.  As just mentioned, an inference method such as Romano and Shaikh
16:777:46940:15:15:86:525:201:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(2008) is applicable to the set identified case.  Akkus, Cookson and Hortacsu (forthcoming) and,
16:778:47036:15:15:86:525:186:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:later, Fox and Bajari (2013, Section VI.B, Appendix C) estimate matching models using single agent
16:779:47134:15:15:86:525:171:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:maximum score estimators using price data and perform Monte Carlo studies. They do not formally
16:780:47229:15:15:86:525:156:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:state assumptions on the competitive equilibrium for an underlying matching model, such as the
16:781:47323:15:15:86:525:141:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:AH model, in order to motivate the consistency of the single agent maximum score estimator using
16:782:47419:15:0:86:205:126:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:primitive assumptions onF
16:783:47444:0:8:208:213:134:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
16:784:47445:8:0:213:234:126:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:-k|j
16:785:47449:0:8:235:240:134:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
16:786:47450:8:15:239:242:126:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:.
16:787:47451:15:15:101:525:111:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The single agent maximum score estimator using data on pricespΩhas many of the same attrac-
16:788:47542:15:0:86:525:96:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tive computational properties as the matching maximum score estimator previewed in Section 2 for
17:789:47640:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:marriage without data on pricespΩ. Most notably, there is no numerical integration over the typically
17:790:47741:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:very long vector-kand no nested algorithm to compute a competitive equilibrium. Also, there is no
17:791:47838:15:0:86:292:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:data curse of dimensionality from estimatingF
17:792:47883:0:8:295:300:673:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
17:793:47884:8:0:300:321:665:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:-k|j
17:794:47888:0:8:322:327:673:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
17:795:47889:8:15:330:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:using a sieve approximation (Chen, 2007) or
17:796:47932:15:15:86:525:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:from estimating choice probabilities ̄Aj(Φ,Ψ)in a nonparametric first stage.9The maximum score
17:797:48026:15:15:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimator using data on prices is consistent ifBis not the set of all sets of trades(Φ,Ψ), which is
17:798:48125:15:15:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:convenient as that set,P(Ω)×P(Ω), is typically quite large in the AH model and other matching
17:799:48218:15:14:86:525:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:models (Fox, 2007). Itemizing all elements ofP(Ω)×P(Ω)is computationally prohibitive in many
17:800:48310:14:15:86:141:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:applications.
17:801:48323:15:15:101:525:576:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Discrete choice models require location and scale normalizations. The scale normalization for single
17:802:48423:15:15:86:525:561:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:agent choice is that the parameters are in monetary units, as the price vectorpΩis observed. This
17:803:48520:15:15:86:525:546:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:scale normalization will change when pricespΩare not observed below. The location normalization
17:804:48615:15:15:86:525:531:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:depends on whether the outside option of making no trades is included in the setB. If not, no constant
17:805:48717:15:15:86:525:516:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:term should be included inX(j,Φ,Ψ)as the constant would be differenced out in the maximum score
17:806:48812:15:15:86:525:501:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:inequalities. If the outside option of making no trades is both observed in the data (agents with no
17:807:48912:15:15:86:525:486:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:trades are measured) and is normalized to have a profit of 0, then a constant term (possibly a separate
17:808:49015:15:15:86:525:471:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:one for different classes of observable agent typesj∈J, such as males and females in marriage) can
17:809:49113:15:31:86:200:456:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:be included inX(j,Φ,Ψ).
17:810:49136:31:22:86:442:425:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:4.2  Nonparametric Identification with Unobservable Prices
17:811:49194:22:15:86:525:403:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f8:Nonparametric identification in a transferable utility matching game seeks to learn aspects ofπj(Φ,Ψ)
17:812:49295:15:15:86:525:388:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:without specifyingπj(Φ,Ψ)up to a finite vector of parametersθ. Nonparametric identification when
17:813:49391:15:15:86:525:373:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:prices of tradespΩare unobservable in the data differs greatly from the analysis of nonparametric
17:814:49488:15:14:86:525:358:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:identification ofπj(Φ,Ψ)in single agent choice under maximum score like assumptions in Matzkin
17:815:49582:14:15:86:391:344:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(1993), at least under the AH model and the separability assumption.
17:816:49650:15:15:101:525:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Loosely speaking, the classic paper of Becker (1973) initiated the study of nonparametric identifi-
17:817:49749:15:15:86:525:314:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:cation of aspects of the valuation functions using data on who matches with whom and where prices
17:818:49846:15:15:86:525:299:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:are present in the model but are not in the data. Becker studied marriage, or one-to-one, two-sided
17:819:49945:15:15:86:525:284:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:matching. In his model, each male and female has a scalar observable type onR, sayjmfor males
17:820:50038:15:15:86:525:269:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:andjffor females. The scalar type could be schooling for males and schooling for females. There
17:821:50133:15:15:86:525:254:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f8:is no unobservable typek. The observed, scalar types enter ajoint valuation functiong(jm,jf)
17:822:50225:15:15:86:526:239:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:that, under transferable utility, is equal toπjm(jf) +πjf(jm), the sum of the valuations of a male
17:823:50323:15:15:86:525:224:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and a female. Becker restricts attention to the case where eitherjmandjfare substitutes or they
17:824:50418:15:23:86:450:209:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:are complements. The scalar types of two matched agents arecomplementswhen
17:825:50492:23:14:271:322:186:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:∂2g(jm,jf)
17:826:50502:14:0:280:312:172:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f13:∂jm∂jf
17:827:50508:0:30:325:341:179:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:>0
17:828:50510:30:15:86:526:149:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:globally andsubstituteswhen the cross-partial derivative is negative. In a special case of the ef-
17:829:50608:15:15:86:525:134:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:ficiency result for the AH model mentioned earlier, Becker shows that complementarities lead to
17:830:50703:15:13:97:525:119:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:9The distributionF(-k|j)is not estimated, as is standard in maximum score. Knowledge of such a distribution
17:831:50810:13:9:86:525:106:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:is needed to compute marginal effects and elasticities. Afterθis estimated using single agent maximum score, a sieve
17:832:50926:9:9:86:525:97:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:maximum likelihood approach (under perhaps stronger assumptions such as no heteroskedasticity) could be used to
17:833:51037:9:0:86:343:88:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:estimate the distribution of-k(Chen, Tamer and Torgovitsky, 2011).
18:834:51105:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f14:positive assortative matching: highjmmales marry highjffemales. Substitutes lead toneg-
18:835:51192:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f4:ative assortative matching. Therefore, if a researcher observes positive assortative matching in
18:836:51288:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the data, then one might conclude that the cross-partial derivative of the joint valuation function is
18:837:51390:15:15:86:469:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:positive. One can identify only the sign of the cross-partial derivative in Becker’s setup.
18:838:51481:15:15:101:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Fox (2010) studies nonparametric identification of joint valuation functions in a two-sided, many-
18:839:51579:15:15:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:to-many matching game using a rank order property for matching games with a finite number of
18:840:51671:15:14:86:525:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:agents. He uses data on who matches with whom but not prices. He extends the intuition in Becker
18:841:51767:14:15:86:525:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:as well as some results in Matzkin (1993) on single agent choice to the many-to-many matching case
18:842:51865:15:15:86:525:576:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:where each agent (or group of agents) has a vector of observable characteristics. For example, one
18:843:51963:15:15:86:525:561:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:can identify the ratio of complementarities (cross partials) on two matched agent characteristics to
18:844:52063:15:15:86:525:546:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the complementarities on two other matched agent characteristics. One identifies the numerical value
18:845:52163:15:15:86:525:531:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of the ratio, not just the sign of the ratio. Identification results vary somewhat depending on whether
18:846:52266:15:15:86:243:516:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:data on unmatched agents are used.
18:847:52300:15:15:101:525:501:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:As Fox (2010) shows for two-sided, many-to-many matching, results on the nonparametric iden-
18:848:52392:15:15:86:525:486:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tification of aspects ofπj(Φ,Ψ)in the AH model using data on trades and not prices do not always
18:849:52488:15:15:86:525:471:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:equal results from using a single agent analysis with data on the prices of tradespΩ(Matzkin, 1993).
18:850:52588:15:15:86:525:456:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:However, the current paper is on tractable semiparametric estimation ofθin the general setting of
18:851:52685:15:15:86:525:441:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the AH model, not nonparametric identification of aspects ofπj(Φ,Ψ)in a more specific setting.
18:852:52779:15:15:86:525:426:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Ideally, the elements ofX(j,Φ,Ψ)should be chosen based on intuition arising from formal results
18:853:52874:15:15:86:525:411:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:on nonparametric identification ofπj(Φ,Ψ)in the special case of the AH model being estimated.
18:854:52967:15:15:86:525:396:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:In what follows, I formally establish only set identification ofθbut am motivated by models where
18:855:53064:15:15:86:525:381:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the elements ofX(j,Φ,Ψ)are specified in such a way that the coming matching maximum score
18:856:53153:15:15:86:525:366:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:inequalities do not always difference out an element of the vectorθ. Without data on prices, a scale
18:857:53253:15:15:86:525:351:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:normalization on the vectorθis needed. I assume that one element ofθis either+1or−1. The sign
18:858:53346:15:31:86:293:336:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:ofθwill typically be identifiable from the data.
18:859:53394:31:21:86:273:305:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:4.3  Matching Maximum Score
18:860:53421:21:15:86:525:284:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:To use a maximum score estimator without data on the prices of tradespΩ, in this subsection I use
18:861:53518:15:15:86:525:269:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:intuition to define matching maximum score inequalities and the matching maximum score objective
18:862:53614:15:15:86:525:254:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:function. In the next subsection, I prove a rank order property for matching without data on prices that
18:863:53718:15:15:86:525:239:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a further result uses to prove that the matching maximum score inequalities lead to set identification
18:864:53820:15:15:86:200:224:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of the parameter vectorθ.
18:865:53845:15:15:101:525:209:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:For intuition, a convenient property of the AH model is that the allocation portionAof any
18:866:53935:15:0:86:189:194:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:competitive equilibrium
18:867:53958:0:8:192:197:202:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
18:868:53959:8:0:197:220:194:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f9:A,pΩ
18:869:53963:0:8:220:225:202:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
18:870:53964:8:15:228:525:194:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:is efficient in the sense of maximizing the social welfare function (6).
18:871:54036:15:15:86:525:179:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Therefore, any other allocation should weakly lower social welfare. First consider the full version of
18:872:54138:15:15:86:525:164:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the AH model where the same pair of two agents can undertake two different trades. In this case,
18:873:54234:15:15:86:526:149:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:we can base an inequality around two specific trades,ω1andω2. The multi-set (allowing duplicates
18:874:54330:15:15:86:525:134:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in the set) of the buyer and seller observable types for tradeω1,b(ω1),s(ω1)∈J, must equal the
18:875:54424:15:15:86:526:119:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:multi-set of the buyer and seller observable types for tradeω2. The buyer observable typeb(ω1)on
18:876:54520:15:15:86:525:104:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tradeω1could be either the buyer or the seller observable type on tradeω2, although a particular
18:877:54616:15:0:86:352:89:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f9:maximum score inequality fixes the role ofb(ω1)on tradeω2
19:878:54675:0:15:101:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The deviation from tradeω1to tradeω2for the two observable typesb(ω1),s(ω1)∈Jis feasible
19:879:54763:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:because there is both a buyer and a seller for each trade under both circumstances. On the left side
19:880:54863:15:0:86:324:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of the inequality, agentb(ω1)conducts the total trades
19:881:54917:0:8:327:332:673:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
19:882:54918:8:0:331:388:665:10:g_d0_f8:7:g_d0_f9:Φb(ω1),Ψb(ω1)
19:883:54931:0:8:389:394:673:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
19:884:54932:8:15:397:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and agents(ω1)conducts the
19:885:54958:15:0:86:136:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:total trades
19:886:54970:0:8:138:143:658:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
19:887:54971:8:0:143:201:650:10:g_d0_f8:7:g_d0_f9:Φs(ω1),Ψs(ω1)
19:888:54984:0:8:201:206:658:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
19:889:54985:8:0:206:262:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:. Further, let
19:890:54999:0:8:265:276:658:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f8:( ̄
19:891:55002:8:0:269:327:650:10:g_d0_f8:7:g_d0_f9:Φs(ω1), ̄Ψb(ω1)
19:892:55017:0:8:327:332:658:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
19:893:55018:8:0:335:351:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and
19:894:55021:0:8:353:364:658:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f8:( ̄
19:895:55024:8:0:358:415:650:10:g_d0_f8:7:g_d0_f9:Φs(ω1), ̄Ψs(ω1)
19:896:55039:0:8:416:421:658:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)

19:898:55064:15:15:86:526:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f14:when the agentsb(ω1),s(ω1)∈Jswitch from tradeω1toω2. Then amatching maximum score
19:899:55145:15:0:86:292:620:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f4:inequalitybased on tradesω1andω2(and on
19:900:55184:0:8:295:300:628:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(

23:1212:67167:14:15:86:525:591:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:-k. However, the proof idea for the rank order property for the semiparametric case originates in
