25:1335:74025:32:21:86:241:469:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:4.7  Truly Finite Markets
25:1336:74050:21:15:86:525:448:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The Azevedo and Hatfield (2015, Section 6) model with a continuum of agents has useful properties.
25:1337:74148:15:15:86:525:433:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A competitive equilibrium always exists and is generically unique without strong restrictions on the
25:1338:74248:15:15:86:525:418:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:valuations of agents. The equivalent to the Azevedo and Hatfield (2015, Section 6) model for a market
25:1339:74349:15:15:86:525:403:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:with atruly finitenumber of agents is the model of Hatfield, Kominers, Nichifor, Ostrovsky and
25:1340:74443:15:15:86:525:388:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Westkamp (2013). I write “truly finite” to emphasize that the issue with finiteness is not about the
25:1341:74543:15:15:86:525:373:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:data; the real equilibrium model in the data generating process has a finite number of agents. A
25:1342:74639:15:14:86:525:358:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:competitive equilibrium to the model of Hatfield et al. (2013) exists if the indirect utility versions of
25:1343:74744:14:15:86:525:344:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f14:the direct utility valuation functionsvi(Φ,Ψ)aresubmodular, what the authors call asubstitutes
25:1344:74838:15:15:86:525:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:condition. In one-to-one matching agents can make only one trade and so valuations are a function
25:1345:74935:15:15:86:525:314:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of a single trade and so trivially submodular. In one-to-many and more complex forms of matching,
25:1346:75032:15:15:86:525:299:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:submodularity of the indirect valuation functions rules out many forms of complementarities across
25:1347:75130:15:15:86:525:284:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:multiple trades involving the same agent, such as the complementarities critical to the empirical
25:1348:75227:15:15:86:525:269:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:study of the car parts industry below. While any competitive equilibrium is efficient and hence the
25:1349:75326:15:15:86:525:254:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:corresponding allocation is unique if the maximizer of the social welfare function is unique, Hatfield
25:1350:75428:15:15:86:525:239:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:et al. demonstrate by example that a failure of the submodularity condition can lead to non-existence
25:1351:75529:15:15:86:212:224:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of a competitive equilibrium.
25:1352:75558:15:15:101:525:209:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:As individual matching markets grow large, the finite-agent model of Hatfield et al. (2013) will
25:1353:75654:15:15:86:525:194:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:presumably converge to the continuum model of Azevedo and Hatfield (2015, Section 6), if the separa-
25:1354:75754:15:15:86:525:179:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:bility assumption is maintained. Therefore, a practical suggestion is to treat the matching maximum
25:1355:75853:15:15:86:525:164:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:score estimator as a large market approximation. Instead, Fox (2010) investigates nonparametric iden-
25:1356:75954:15:12:93:525:149:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:16For the example of single agent binary choice, sufficient conditions for set identification in the maximum score model
25:1357:76074:12:10:86:525:137:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:of Manski (1975) allow for heteroskedasticity (hereF(-k|j)varies withj) while known sufficient conditions for set
25:1358:76187:10:9:86:525:127:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:identification in the maximum rank correlation model of Han (1987), applied to binary choice, require homoskedasticity
25:1359:76305:9:10:86:525:118:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:(hereF(-k|j)does not vary withj). In matching, the “maximum score” and “maximum rank correlation” asymptotic
25:1360:76413:10:9:86:525:108:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:arguments both allow for heteroskedasticity, based on the rank order property in Proposition 1. The proof of Proposition
25:1361:76533:9:10:86:525:99:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:1 relies on the properties of competitive equilibrium and so the theorem is not an analog to the conditions for set
25:1362:76648:10:0:86:256:89:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:identification for binary choice in Han (1987).
26:1363:76697:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tification of aspects of the many-to-many joint valuation function in a truly finite market setting by
26:1364:76799:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:imposing a rank order property for matching without data on prices for the truly finite market setting.
26:1365:76902:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:While Fox does not discuss estimation or derive a rank order property using primitive conditions on
26:1366:77001:15:15:86:525:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the distribution of unobservables, the rank order property in Fox would lead to the consistency of the
26:1367:77103:15:15:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:matching maximum score estimator in a truly finite market setting. That rank order property can
26:1368:77198:15:37:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:also be applied to the case where the market is truly finite but not all agents are recorded in the data.
26:1369:77303:37:25:86:242:583:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:5  Car Parts Industry
26:1370:77324:25:15:86:525:558:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I now present an empirical application about the matching of assemblers to car parts suppliers in the
26:1371:77425:15:15:86:525:543:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:automobile industry. Automobile assemblers are well-known, large manufacturers, such as BMW, Ford
26:1372:77522:15:15:86:525:528:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:or Honda. Automotive suppliers are less well-known to the public, and range from large companies
26:1373:77618:15:15:86:525:513:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:such as Bosch to smaller firms that specialize in one type of car part.  A car is one of the most
26:1374:77715:15:15:86:525:498:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:complicated manufacturing goods sold to individual consumers. Making a car be both high quality
26:1375:77810:15:14:86:525:483:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and inexpensive is a technical challenge. Developing the supply chain is an important part of that
26:1376:77908:14:15:86:525:469:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:challenge. More so than in many other manufacturing industries, suppliers in the automobile industry
26:1377:78008:15:15:86:500:454:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:receive a large amount of coverage in the industry press because of their economic importance.
26:1378:78102:15:15:101:525:439:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A matching opportunity in the automotive industry is an individual car part that is needed for
26:1379:78196:15:15:86:525:424:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a car model. A particular tradeω∈Ωencodes an individual car part that is needed for a named
26:1380:78287:15:15:86:525:409:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:car model as well as buyer and seller observable types. Each car model itself has a brand. For the
26:1381:78385:15:15:86:525:394:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Chevrolet Impala, Chevrolet is the brand and Impala is the model. There are multiple consummated
26:1382:78481:15:15:86:526:379:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tradesωfor the Chevrolet Impala because each model uses multiple parts. Finally, each brand is
26:1383:78575:15:15:86:525:364:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:owned by an assembler, in Chevrolet’s case General Motors. General Motors is the buyer observable
26:1384:78672:15:15:86:525:349:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:typeb(ω)∈Jon all the trades for car parts used on the Chevrolet Impala. The seller observable
26:1385:78765:15:15:86:525:334:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:types(ω)∈Jon each trade is a particular car parts supplier, like Bosch. Therefore, each named
26:1386:78858:15:15:86:525:319:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:firm represents a separate observable type in the AH model.17In the AH model, there is one trade
26:1387:78954:15:15:86:525:304:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:ω∈Ωfor the windshield on the Chevrolet Impala for each suppliers(ω)that supplies at least one
26:1388:79047:15:15:86:525:289:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:windshield for any of the models in the data and so could (according to the model) counterfactually
26:1389:79146:15:15:86:250:274:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:supply the windshield for the Impala.
26:1390:79183:15:15:101:525:259:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I refer to Example 2 and model the car parts industry as an explicitly two-sided market, where
26:1391:79277:15:15:86:525:244:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:each supplier conducts trades only as a seller and each assembler conducts trades only as a buyer.
26:1392:79375:15:15:86:525:229:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:From an automotive engineering perspective, an assembler needs a specific set of car parts to make
26:1393:79473:15:14:86:525:214:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a particular model. For example, each car model needs a single windshield.18For an assembleri,
26:1394:79567:14:15:86:525:200:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:definevi(Φ) =−∞for any set of tradesΦthat do not contain exactly one trade for every car part
26:1395:79660:15:15:86:525:185:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:opportunity in the data.  On the right side of a matching maximum score inequality (10), I drop
26:1396:79755:15:0:86:176:170:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f13:inequalities wherevi
26:1397:79775:0:8:178:189:178:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f8:( ̄
26:1398:79778:8:0:183:190:170:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:Φ
26:1399:79779:0:8:190:195:178:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
26:1400:79780:8:15:198:525:170:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f4:=−∞. Therefore, a counterfactual tradeω3corresponds to, for example,
26:1401:79848:15:15:86:525:155:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:General Motors using a different supplier for the windshield for the Chevrolet Impala, not General
26:1402:79946:15:12:93:525:140:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:17The economic questions considered here focus on supplier and assembler specialization and so I need to allow each
26:1403:80061:12:10:86:525:128:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:firm to be its own observable typej∈Jto properly measure specialization. The AH model uses a finite number of
26:1404:80170:10:9:86:525:118:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:tradesω∈Ωand a continuum of full agent typesi∈I. In my empirical version of the AH model, the number of
26:1405:80273:9:10:86:525:109:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:observable typesj∈Jis also finite. Here, the fiction mapping the continuum AH model to the finite data is that there
26:1406:80389:10:9:86:100:99:8:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f6:is a continuum of firms of the General Motors observable type but only one such firm is sampled in the data.18
26:1407:80499:9:0:101:442:90:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:The data do not report back up or secondary suppliers for a part on a particular car model.
27:1408:80592:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Motors installing two different windshields on the Chevrolet Impala or replacing the windshield with
27:1409:80692:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a tire. By the market definition discussed below, only suppliers that make at least one windshield in
27:1410:80793:15:15:86:526:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the data can be the seller observable type on the counterfactual tradeω3in a matching maximum
27:1411:80886:15:15:86:354:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:score inequality (10) based on swapping windshield suppliers.
27:1412:80947:15:15:101:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The car parts data come from SupplierBusiness, an analyst firm. I merge them with car sales data
27:1413:81043:15:15:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:collected from several sources for the United States and several large countries in Western Europe. I
27:1414:81144:15:14:86:525:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:focus on 30 large component categories, such as air conditioning parts, body parts and transmission
27:1415:81243:14:15:86:525:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:parts. In the merged and cleaned data, there are 941 suppliers, 11 assemblers (parent companies),
27:1416:81340:15:15:86:525:576:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:46 car brands, 260 car models, and 34,836 car parts. While the data cover different model years, for
27:1417:81440:15:15:86:525:561:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:simplicity I ignore the time dimension and treat each market as clearing simultaneously.19I treat each
27:1418:81542:15:15:86:525:546:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:component category as a statistically independent matching market.20Therefore, I use the matching
27:1419:81639:15:15:86:371:531:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:maximum score objective function for multiple markets in (15).21
27:1420:81703:15:15:101:525:516:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:One of the empirical applications focuses on General Motors divesting Opel, a brand it owns in
27:1421:81797:15:15:86:525:501:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Europe. In order to model the interdependence of the European and North American operations of
27:1422:81891:15:15:86:525:486:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:General Motors and suppliers to General Motors, the definition of a matching market is car parts
27:1423:81987:15:15:86:525:471:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in a particular component category used in cars assembled in Europe and North America.  Most
27:1424:82079:15:15:86:525:456:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of the assemblers and many of the larger suppliers operate on multiple continents.22However, the
27:1425:82175:15:15:86:525:441:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:point estimates found when splitting Europe and North America into separate matching markets are
27:1426:82271:15:15:86:525:426:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:similar to those presented here, suggesting that geographic market definitions do not play a large role
27:1427:82374:15:15:86:525:411:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in identifying the parameters. Note that many of the estimated gains to specialization to a supplier
27:1428:82474:15:15:86:525:396:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:likely come from plant co-location: using one supplier plant to supply the same type of car part to
27:1429:82573:15:15:86:525:381:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:multiple car models assembled in the same plant or in nearby plants. Thus, an empirical regularity
27:1430:82671:15:15:86:525:366:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of certain suppliers being more prevalent in one continent than another is consistent with the gains
27:1431:82771:15:15:86:526:351:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:to specialization that I seek to estimate.23The data have poor coverage for car models assembled in
27:1432:82870:15:14:86:525:336:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Asia, so I cannot include the corresponding car parts in the empirical work. I do focus heavily on car
27:1433:82972:14:15:86:525:322:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:parts used on cars assembled in Europe and North America by assemblers with headquarters in Asia.
27:1434:83069:15:15:101:525:307:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The automotive supplier empirical application is a good showcase for the strengths of the matching
27:1435:83167:15:15:86:525:292:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:maximum score estimator. The matching markets modeled here contain many more agents than the
27:1436:83259:15:15:86:525:277:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:markets modeled in many non-marriage papers on estimating matching games. The computational
27:1437:83350:15:15:86:525:262:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:simplicity of maximum score, or some other approach that avoids repeated computations of model
27:1438:83444:15:15:86:525:247:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:outcomes, is needed here.  I focus on specialization in the portfolio of matches for suppliers and
27:1439:83542:15:9:93:303:232:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:19Car models are refreshed around once every five years.
27:1440:83598:9:13:93:525:223:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:20The same supplier may appear in multiple component categories, and so a researcher might want to model spillovers
27:1441:83713:13:9:86:525:210:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:across component categories. Pooling component categories into one large market creates no new issues with the AH
27:1442:83826:9:10:86:525:201:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:model or the matching maximum score estimator. The history of the industry shows that many US suppliers were
27:1443:83934:10:9:86:525:191:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:formed in the 1910’s and 1920’s around Detroit (Klier and Rubenstein, 2008). Some firms chose to specialize in one or
27:1444:84051:9:10:86:525:182:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:a few component categories and others specialized in more component categories. The particular historical pattern of
27:1445:84167:10:9:86:100:172:8:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f6:what component categories each supplier produces lies outside of the scope of this investigation.21
27:1446:84266:9:9:101:525:163:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:The parameter estimates in this paper would presumably change if SupplierBusiness aggregated or disaggregated
27:1447:84375:9:7:86:285:154:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:car parts into component categories in different ways.
27:1448:84429:7:12:93:525:147:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:22Nissan and Renault are treated as one assembler because of their deep integration. Chrysler and Daimler were part
27:1449:84544:12:7:86:281:135:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:of the same assembler during the period of the data.
27:1450:84596:7:12:93:525:128:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:23A few suppliers are owned by assemblers. I ignore the vertical integration decision in my analysis, in part because
27:1451:84713:12:10:86:525:116:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:I lack data on supplier ownership and in part because vertical integration is just an extreme version of specialization,
27:1452:84833:10:9:86:525:106:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:the focus of my investigation. If a supplier sends car parts to only one assembler, that data are recorded and used
27:1453:84948:9:10:86:525:97:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:as endogenous matching outcomes.  Vertical integration in automobile manufacturing has been studied previously
27:1454:85058:10:0:86:415:87:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:(Monteverde and Teece, 1982; Novak and Eppinger, 2001; Novak and Stern, 2008, 2009).
28:1455:85144:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:assemblers. Along with my related use of the estimator introduced here in Fox and Bajari (2013),
28:1456:85240:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:an earlier draft of the current paper was the first empirical application to a many-to-many matching
28:1457:85340:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:market where the valuation from a set of matches (or trades) is not additively separable across the
28:1458:85439:15:15:86:525:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:individual matches. Finally, the prices of the car parts are not in publicly available data. The matching
28:1459:85544:15:15:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimator does not require data on the prices of trades, even though prices are present in the economic
28:1460:85647:15:37:86:187:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:model being estimated.
28:1461:85669:37:27:86:373:583:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:6  Costs of Assemblers Divesting Brands
28:1462:85708:27:22:86:268:556:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:6.1  General Motors and Opel
28:1463:85736:22:15:86:525:534:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:In 2009, General Motors (GM), the world’s largest automobile assembler for most of the twentieth
28:1464:85832:15:15:86:525:519:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:century, declared bankruptcy. As part of the bankruptcy process, GM divested or eliminated several
28:1465:85930:15:15:86:525:504:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of its brands, including Pontiac and Saturn in North America and SAAB in Europe. Economists know
28:1466:86026:15:14:86:525:489:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:little about the benefits and costs of large assemblers in the globally integrated automobile industry
28:1467:86128:14:15:86:525:475:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:divesting brands. This paper seeks to use the matching patterns in the car parts industry to estimate
28:1468:86229:15:15:86:249:460:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:one aspect of the costs of divestment.
28:1469:86267:15:15:101:525:445:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A major public policy issue during 2009 was whether General Motors should also divest its largest
28:1470:86364:15:15:86:525:430:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:European brands, Opel and Vauxhall.24Opel is based in Germany and Vauxhall is based in the United
28:1471:86461:15:15:86:525:415:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Kingdom. Consistent with the close link between Opel and Vauxhall, they will be grouped together
28:1472:86557:15:15:86:525:400:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:as one brand, Opel, in the empirical work. Over the period of the data, Opel also had assembly plants
28:1473:86658:15:15:86:269:385:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in Belgium, Hungary, Poland, and Russia.
28:1474:86698:15:15:101:525:370:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A major advocate of GM divesting Opel was the German government, which desired to protect
28:1475:86787:15:15:86:525:355:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:jobs at Opel assembly plants, at Opel dealers and at suppliers to Opel, but was reluctant to subsidize
28:1476:86889:15:15:86:525:340:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a bankrupt North American firm. During most of 2009, the presumption by GM was that Opel would
28:1477:86983:15:15:86:525:325:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:be divested. Indeed, GM held an auction and agreed to sell Opel to a consortium from Canada and
28:1478:87078:15:15:86:525:310:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Russia. In November 2009, GM canceled the sale and kept Opel as an integrated subsidiary of GM.
28:1479:87173:15:15:86:525:295:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Opel and the North American operations of GM share many common platforms for basing individual
28:1480:87267:15:15:86:525:280:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:models on. One reason for keeping Opel integrated is that a larger, global assembler will have gains
28:1481:87367:15:15:86:525:265:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:from specialization in its own assembly plants and in the plants of suppliers. Increasing the gains to
28:1482:87469:15:15:86:525:250:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:suppliers from specializing in producing car parts for GM may indirectly benefit GM through lower
28:1483:87566:15:31:86:171:235:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:prices for car parts.
28:1484:87587:31:21:86:359:204:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:6.2  Valuation Functions of Observable Types
28:1485:87631:21:15:86:525:183:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:This section estimates the parameters in the valuation functions over observable types for assemblers
28:1486:87732:15:15:86:525:168:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and suppliers for the portfolio of car part trades each firm buys or sells. Let the notation for the
28:1487:87832:15:15:86:525:153:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f13:observable typejsemphasize that the firm in question is a supper or seller and the notationjb
28:1488:87925:15:15:86:525:138:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:emphasize that the firm is a buyer or assembler, as the car parts industry is an explicitly two-sided
28:1489:88026:15:0:86:249:123:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f13:market. I use the functional formsπθ
28:1490:88062:0:8:251:256:131:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(

28:1494:88070:0:8:305:310:131:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(

28:1497:88077:8:16:339:525:123:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f13:θbfor buyers andπθ(js,Ψ) =X(js,Ψ)′θs
28:1498:88113:16:0:93:482:107:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:24GM has owned Opel since 1929, although its control temporarily lapsed during the second World War.
29:1499:88215:0:0:86:171:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f8:for sellers, withθ=

29:1505:88272:8:0:349:369:695:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:jb,Φ
29:1506:88276:0:8:369:374:703:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
29:1507:88277:8:15:377:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:andX(js,Ψ)are measures of how
29:1508:88306:15:29:86:359:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:specialized each portfolio of car part trades is at several levels.
29:1509:88373:29:21:86:289:651:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f14:6.2.1  Valuation Functions for Suppliers
29:1510:88413:21:15:86:525:630:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:For suppliers,X(js,Ψ)tracks specialization in four areas: parts (in the same component category)
29:1511:88509:15:15:86:525:615:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for an individual car, parts for cars from a particular brand (Chevrolet, Audi), parts for cars from a
29:1512:88611:15:15:86:525:600:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:particular parent company or assembler (General Motors, Volkswagen) and parts for cars for brands
29:1513:88708:15:15:86:419:585:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:with headquarters on a particular continent (Asia, Europe, North America).
29:1514:88782:15:15:101:525:570:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The choice of a measure of specialization is somewhat arbitrary. I use the Herfindahl-Hirschman
29:1515:88877:15:15:86:525:555:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Index (HHI) because economists are familiar with its units, which range between 0 and 1. For example,
29:1516:88978:15:15:86:525:540:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:say the North American firms of Chrysler, General Motors and Ford are the only three assemblers.
29:1517:89074:15:32:86:480:525:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Then the corresponding parent group scalar elementXPG(js,Ψ)of the vectorX(js,Ψ)is
29:1518:89155:32:0:99:160:493:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:XPG(js,Ψ) =
29:1519:89166:0:7:163:170:507:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
29:1520:89167:7:14:172:262:500:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:# Chrysler parts in Ψ
29:1521:89188:14:0:180:254:486:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:# total parts in Ψ
29:1522:89206:0:14:263:274:507:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f9:)2
29:1523:89208:14:0:277:285:493:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:+
29:1524:89209:0:7:287:294:507:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
29:1525:89210:7:14:296:369:500:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:# Ford parts in Ψ
29:1526:89227:14:0:296:370:486:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:# total parts in Ψ
29:1527:89245:0:14:370:382:507:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f9:)2
29:1528:89247:14:0:385:393:493:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:+
29:1529:89248:0:7:394:401:507:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
29:1530:89249:7:14:405:475:500:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:# GM parts in Ψ
29:1531:89264:14:0:403:477:486:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:# total parts in Ψ
29:1532:89282:0:14:478:489:507:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f9:)2
29:1533:89284:14:30:491:525:493:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:.(16)
29:1534:89289:30:15:86:525:463:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:As this specialization measure enters the valuation function for a supplier,XPG(js,Ψ)is 1 if the
29:1535:89385:15:15:86:525:448:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:supplier sells parts only to, say, GM and 1/3 if it sells an equal number of parts to each assembler.
29:1536:89486:15:15:86:525:433:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The use of the HHI differs from antitrust; here the HHI is a measure of specialization for a portfolio
29:1537:89588:15:15:86:525:418:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f4:Ψof car part trades for a particular supplierjsand is not a measure of concentration in the overall
29:1538:89687:15:15:86:525:403:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:industry for car parts. The specialization measureXPG(js,Ψ)can be computed both for the trades
29:1539:89781:15:15:86:525:388:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f4:Ψfor a supplier in the data and in the counterfactual trades in a matching maximum score inequality
29:1540:89880:15:15:86:114:373:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:(10).25
29:1541:89887:15:15:101:525:358:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:When I consider the counterfactual of GM divesting Opel and making it an independent assembler
29:1542:89981:15:15:86:525:343:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:or parent company, the changes in total valuation will be generated by the estimated parameter
29:1543:90075:15:15:86:525:328:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:on the importance of specialization at the parent company level, relative to the values of the other
29:1544:90175:15:15:86:137:313:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:parameters.
29:1545:90186:15:15:101:525:298:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The pattern of sorting across trades in the car parts market is used to measure the relative
29:1546:90278:15:15:86:525:283:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:importance of specializing at different levels of aggregation. The management literature has suggested
29:1547:90380:15:15:86:525:268:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:that supplier specialization may be a key driver of assembler performance (Dyer, 1996, 1997; Novak
29:1548:90478:15:15:86:184:253:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and Wernerfelt, 2012).
29:1549:90500:15:15:101:525:238:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:By construction, two parts for the same car model also have the same brand, parent group and
29:1550:90592:15:15:86:525:223:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:continent. Two car parts for cars from the same brand are automatically in the same parent group and
29:1551:90692:15:14:86:525:208:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the brand only has one headquarters, so the parts are from a brand with a headquarters in the same
29:1552:90790:14:15:86:525:194:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:continent as well. Two cars from the same parent group are not necessarily from the same continent,
29:1553:90889:15:15:86:464:179:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:as Opel is a European brand of GM and Chevrolet is a North American brand of GM.
29:1554:90969:15:16:101:525:164:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The four specialization measures inX(js,Ψ)are highly correlated. Just as univariate linear least
29:1555:91065:16:12:93:525:148:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:25Many other upstream firm characteristics would be endogenous at the level of the competitive equilibrium considered
29:1556:91182:12:9:86:525:136:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:here. For example, many of the benefits of specialization occur through plant co-location and so suppliers and assembler
29:1557:91302:9:10:86:525:127:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:plant locations should be considered endogenous matching outcomes rather than exogenous firm characteristics. With
29:1558:91416:10:9:86:525:117:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:just-in-time production at many assembly sites, supplier factories are built short distances away so parts can be produced
29:1559:91538:9:10:86:525:108:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:and shipped to the assembly site within hours, in many cases. Plant location could be added as an extra element to a
29:1560:91654:10:0:86:168:98:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:tradeωin other work.
30:1561:91676:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:squares applied to each covariate separately produces different slope coefficients than multivariate
30:1562:91776:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:linear least squares when the covariates are correlated, a univariate matching theoretic analysis (such
30:1563:91879:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:as Becker (1973)) on each measure inX(js,Ψ)separately will be inadequate here.  A univariate
30:1564:91971:15:15:86:525:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:analysis of sayXPG(js,Ψ)would just amount to saying that the corresponding element ofθis positive
30:1565:92068:15:15:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:when each supplier does more business with certain parent groups than others. In principle, even this
30:1566:92169:15:15:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:conclusion about the sign of the parameter could be wrong if the correlation with the other three
30:1567:92266:15:14:86:525:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:characteristics is not considered in estimation. Here I measure the relative importance of each of the
30:1568:92368:14:29:86:441:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:four types of specialization: at which level do the returns to specialization occur?
30:1569:92452:29:22:86:299:562:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f14:6.2.2  Valuation Functions for Assemblers
30:1570:92493:22:15:86:525:540:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The valuation function of assemblers has a similar functional form, focusing on specializing in a small
30:1571:92596:15:15:86:525:525:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:number of suppliers. LetΦbe a portfolio of car part trades for buyer or assemblerjb. I consider
30:1572:92691:15:0:86:348:510:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:parent group, brand and model specialization in the vectorX
30:1573:92750:0:8:351:356:518:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
30:1574:92751:8:0:355:375:510:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:jb,Φ
30:1575:92755:0:8:375:380:518:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
30:1576:92756:8:15:380:525:510:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:. For conciseness, I do not include
30:1577:92791:15:15:86:390:495:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a term for specialization at the continent of brand headquarters level.
30:1578:92862:15:14:101:525:480:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Consider the Herfindahl index for the concentration of suppliers selling parts to an assembler.
30:1579:92957:14:15:86:525:466:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Given a portfolioΦ, lets(Φ)be the set of distinct suppliers who sell at least one car part trade inΦ.
30:1580:93058:15:30:86:183:451:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Then define the scalar
30:1581:93080:30:0:184:204:421:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f9:XPG
30:1582:93083:0:8:205:210:429:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
30:1583:93084:8:0:210:230:421:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:jb,Φ
30:1584:93088:0:8:230:235:429:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
30:1585:93089:8:0:238:246:421:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:=
30:1586:93090:0:22:253:267:430:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:∑
30:1587:93091:22:0:248:272:408:7:g_d0_f13:7:g_d0_f9:i∈s(Φ)
30:1588:93097:0:8:274:281:435:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
30:1589:93098:8:13:282:410:427:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:# trades sold by supplieriin Φ
30:1590:93128:13:0:307:385:414:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:# total trades in Φ
30:1591:93147:0:14:411:423:435:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f9:)2
30:1592:93149:14:37:425:428:421:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:.
30:1593:93150:37:0:86:130:384:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f9:Next,XBr
30:1594:93158:0:8:131:136:392:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
30:1595:93159:8:0:136:156:384:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:jb,Φ
30:1596:93163:0:8:156:161:392:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
30:1597:93164:8:15:163:525:384:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:is the mean of such a Herfindahl index computed for each brand separately. Consider
30:1598:93247:15:15:86:525:369:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:GM and say that the only two brands of GM are Chevrolet (Chevy) and Opel and lets(Φ,Opel)be
30:1599:93338:15:35:86:354:354:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the set of suppliers selling parts to Opel inΦ. Then, for GM,
30:1600:93399:35:0:96:125:319:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f9:XBrand
30:1601:93405:0:8:128:133:327:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(

30:1603:93410:0:8:153:158:327:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
30:1604:93411:8:0:160:168:319:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:=

30:1612:93493:0:50:394:406:333:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f9:)2
30:1613:93495:50:0:235:243:283:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:+
30:1614:93496:0:13:246:251:290:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:1
30:1615:93497:13:0:246:251:277:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:2
30:1616:93498:0:22:271:285:293:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:∑
30:1617:93499:22:0:254:302:271:7:g_d0_f13:7:g_d0_f9:i∈s(Φ,Chevy)
30:1618:93511:0:7:304:311:297:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
30:1619:93512:7:13:312:480:290:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:# trades sold by supplierito Chevy in Φ
30:1620:93551:13:0:336:457:277:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:# total trades for Chevy in Φ
30:1621:93580:0:14:481:493:297:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f9:)2
30:1622:93582:14:37:495:525:283:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:.(17)
30:1623:93587:37:0:86:159:246:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f9:Likewise,XModel
30:1624:93602:0:8:160:165:254:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
30:1625:93603:8:0:165:185:246:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:jb,Φ
30:1626:93607:0:8:185:190:254:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
30:1627:93608:8:15:193:525:246:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:is the mean across car models sold by GM of the Herfindahl index calculated
30:1628:93683:15:0:86:475:231:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:for the sellers of parts to each car model separately. As with suppliers, the elements ofX
30:1629:93773:0:8:477:482:239:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
30:1630:93774:8:0:482:502:231:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:jb,Φ
30:1631:93778:0:8:502:507:239:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
30:1632:93779:8:15:510:525:231:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:can
30:1633:93782:15:15:86:490:216:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:be computed for the counterfactual trades in the matching maximum score inequalities (10).
30:1634:93872:15:14:101:525:201:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The matching maximum score inequalities used in estimation keep the number of car part trades
30:1635:93965:14:15:86:525:187:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:sold by each supplier (and, more obviously, the set of car parts needed on each car model) the same.
30:1636:94065:15:15:86:525:172:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:With strong returns to specialization, it may be more efficient to have fewer but individually larger
30:1637:94166:15:15:86:525:157:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:suppliers. The optimality of supplier size is not imposed as part of the estimator. Nor can the gains
30:1638:94267:15:15:86:525:142:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:from assembler scale be identified from matching maximum score inequalities where each car part and
30:1639:94366:15:15:86:525:127:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:each car model are weighted equally. This paper models the car parts industry, not the market for
30:1640:94463:15:15:86:525:112:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:corporate control of car brands and car models. Not imposing the optimality of supplier and assembler
30:1641:94564:15:0:86:525:97:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:sizes might be an advantage, as other concerns such as capacity constraints and antitrust rules could
31:1642:94667:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:limit firm size. On the other hand, one of the benefits of GM not divesting Opel is keeping a larger
31:1643:94767:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:scale, and the matching maximum score inequalities used in estimation do not identify a pure scale
31:1644:94865:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:economy for GM owning Opel. Instead, the matching maximum score inequalities focus on the gains
31:1645:94960:15:31:86:525:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:to assemblers and particularly to suppliers from specialization, for a fixed number of car part trades.
31:1646:95063:31:21:86:317:619:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:6.3  Estimates for Valuation Functions
31:1647:95101:21:15:86:525:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Table 1 presents the point estimates and confidence intervals for the parameter vectorθin the valuation
31:1648:95204:15:15:86:525:583:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:functions for observable types, for both assemblers and suppliers. I randomly sample a maximum of
31:1649:95301:15:15:86:525:568:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:10,000 matching maximum score inequalities (10) per component category.  All theoretically valid
31:1650:95397:15:15:86:525:553:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:inequalities with two different suppliers are sampled with an equal probability. I use the set identified
31:1651:95502:15:15:86:525:538:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:subsampling procedure of Romano and Shaikh (2008) to construct confidence regions. See Appendix
31:1652:95597:15:15:86:266:523:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B for details on estimation and inference.
31:1653:95639:15:15:101:525:508:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The parameter on assembler (parent group) specialization for suppliers is normalized to be±1. The
31:1654:95736:15:15:86:525:493:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:other parameters in Table 1 are interpreted relative to the parameter on parent group specialization.
31:1655:95837:15:15:86:525:478:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:One finding in that the point estimates of the assembler parameters have a much lower order of
31:1656:95931:15:15:86:525:463:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:magnitude than the supplier parameters and the parameters have wide confidence bands, always
31:1657:96023:15:15:86:525:448:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:including 0. For assemblers, the upper bounds of the confidence bands for parent group, brand and
31:1658:96120:15:15:86:525:433:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:model specialization are lower than the lower bounds for the analogous specialization measures for
31:1659:96218:15:15:86:525:418:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:suppliers.  Therefore, for these specialization measures one can at least statistically conclude that
31:1660:96319:15:15:86:525:403:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:supplier specialization measures are more important.  This difference between the point estimates
31:1661:96416:15:0:86:426:388:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:for assemblers and suppliers is not because of a difference in the units ofX
31:1662:96492:0:8:429:434:396:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
31:1663:96493:8:0:433:453:388:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:jb,Φ
31:1664:96497:0:8:454:459:396:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
31:1665:96498:8:15:462:525:388:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:andX(js,Ψ);
31:1666:96509:15:15:86:525:373:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the rightmost columns of Table 1 report the means and standard deviations of the specialization
31:1667:96604:15:14:86:525:358:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:measures for realized matches for both suppliers and assemblers. The specialization (HHI) measures
31:1668:96702:14:15:86:525:344:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:are about the same magnitudes for both suppliers and assemblers. What is possibly explaining the
31:1669:96798:15:15:86:525:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:small magnitude effects is that two economic forces may offset each other: assemblers prefer to have a
31:1670:96900:15:15:86:525:314:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:diverse supplier base to avoid placing their success in the hands of one supplier (hold up) while there
31:1671:97003:15:15:86:525:299:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:may be some manufacturing benefits from having a fewer number of suppliers. Regardless, the point
31:1672:97100:15:15:86:525:284:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimates show that assembler specialization is much less important than supplier specialization in
31:1673:97199:15:15:86:525:269:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the valuation functions. One caveat is that the confidence intervals for assembler specialization at the
31:1674:97303:15:15:86:401:254:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:model levels do contain larger, in absolute value, coefficient magnitudes.
31:1675:97377:15:15:101:525:239:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:For suppliers, Table 1 shows that all four coefficients on supplier specialization are positive, meaning
31:1676:97481:15:15:86:525:224:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:as expected specialization on these dimensions increases the valuation of suppliers. The point estimates
31:1677:97585:15:15:86:525:209:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:show that a given level of specialization at the parent-group level is about as important in valuation
31:1678:97687:15:15:86:525:194:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:as the same level of specialization at the continent-of-brand-headquarters level. At the same time, the
31:1679:97790:15:15:86:525:179:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:standard deviation of parent-group-specialization HHI, across realized matches, is 0.18, meaning the
31:1680:97890:15:15:86:525:164:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:variation in parent-group specialization across suppliers is lower than for some other specialization
31:1681:97991:15:15:86:525:149:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:measures. A naive researcher might be inclined to interpret this level of dispersion as evidence parent-
31:1682:98095:15:15:86:525:134:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:group specialization is unimportant. This would be wrong: the matching maximum score estimator
31:1683:98189:15:15:86:525:119:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:accounts for the fact that more available matching opportunities occur across firm boundaries than
31:1684:98287:15:15:86:525:104:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:within them. An estimate of a structural parameter such as the coefficient on parent group tells us
31:1685:98386:15:0:86:387:89:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the importance of parent group in the valuation from a set of trades.
32:1686:98457:0:15:101:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Table 1 also shows that supplier specialization at the brand and model levels is even more important
32:1687:98557:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:than specialization at the parent-group level, as the brand and model confidence intervals do not
32:1688:98654:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:contain +1. The high point estimate of 376 for model specialization possibly comes from supplier and
32:1689:98754:15:15:86:525:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:assembler plant co-location: car models of even the same brand may be built in separate plants and
32:1690:98852:15:15:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:some benefits from specialization may occur from saving on the need to have multiple supplier plants
32:1691:98952:15:15:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for each model. Also, the technological compatibility of car parts occurs mainly at the model level.
32:1692:99052:15:14:86:525:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Notice how the standard deviation of the HHI-specialization measure is about the same (0.26–0.28)
32:1693:99149:14:15:86:525:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for the continent, brand and model measures, with parent group specialization being a little lower
32:1694:99247:15:15:86:525:576:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:at 0.18. Again, naive researchers might use the HHI means to conclude that specialization at the
32:1695:99343:15:15:86:525:561:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:model level is less important or use the standard deviations to conclude that specialization at the
32:1696:99442:15:15:86:525:546:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:continent, brand and model levels are equally important. The estimates of the valuation functions
32:1697:99539:15:15:86:525:531:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:give statistically consistent estimates of the relative importance of the types of specialization in the
32:1698:99643:15:15:86:283:516:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:valuation functions for supplier relationships.
32:1699:99690:15:15:101:525:501:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Table 1 also shows that there are 298,272 inequalities used in estimation. Of those, 82% are satisfied
32:1700:99792:15:15:86:525:486:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:at the reported point estimates. The fraction of satisfied inequalities is a measure of statistical fit.
32:1701:99896:15:15:86:525:471:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Appendix C presents estimates where the HHI specialization measures use different weighting schemes,
32:1702:99996:15:15:86:525:456:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:including weighting schemes using data on car model sales in Europe and North America.  The
32:1703:100087:15:15:86:525:441:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:specifications in Appendix C result in lower numbers of inequalities being satisfied at the parameter
32:1704:100188:15:15:86:525:426:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimates. Therefore, these alternatives result in statistically worse fit and so are not presented in the
32:1705:100294:15:15:86:525:411:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:main text. However, a common finding in Appendix C is that the assembler parameters become more
32:1706:100389:15:31:86:405:396:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:important, particularly the parameter on assembler model specialization.
32:1707:100461:31:21:86:412:365:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:6.4  Supplier Valuation Loss From GM Divesting Opel
32:1708:100512:21:15:86:525:344:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Encouraging General Motors to divest Opel was a major policy issue in Germany during 2009. The
32:1709:100606:15:15:86:525:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:revealed preference of GM to back away from selling Opel to outside investors suggests that GM felt
32:1710:100705:15:15:86:525:314:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:that Opel was important to its performance. One possibility is that GM feared a loss of economies
32:1711:100802:15:15:86:525:299:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of scale (total size) or scope (strength in fuel efficient cars that could be transferred from Europe to
32:1712:100906:15:15:86:525:284:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:North America, say) from such a divestiture. Matching in the car parts industry is not necessarily
32:1713:101004:15:15:86:341:269:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:informative about assembler economies of scale and scope.
32:1714:101061:15:15:101:525:254:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Using information from the car parts industry, and in particular in light of the minuscule point
32:1715:101157:15:15:86:525:239:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimates on assembler specialization above, the major estimated effect of GM divesting Opel will
32:1716:101254:15:15:86:525:224:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:come from suppliers to GM being less specialized as GM’s and Opel’s models technologically diverge.
32:1717:101353:15:15:86:525:209:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:This will hurt GM through equilibrium prices of trades: suppliers will charge higher prices to GM
32:1718:101450:15:15:86:525:194:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for car parts.  In each component category, I construct the counterfactual sum of valuations from
32:1719:101547:15:15:86:525:179:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:observable types to suppliers if Opel and the rest of GM are now treated as separate assemblers, or
32:1720:101646:15:15:86:525:164:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:parent groups. The same sellers supply the same car part trades to the same car models, but now the
32:1721:101745:15:15:86:525:149:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Opel models are produced by an independent parent group. In (16), some car parts are transferred to a
32:1722:101846:15:15:86:525:134:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:new parent group and so the measure of parent group specialization weakly decreases for any supplier
32:1723:101946:15:15:86:525:119:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f8:that sells any parts to Opel. The decrease in the parent group specialization measureXPG(js,Ψ)
32:1724:102040:15:0:86:526:104:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:times its estimated parameterθsPGgives the decrease in the valuation for each supplier who sells at
33:1725:102141:0:23:86:369:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:least one part to Opel. I focus on a percentage decrease measure
33:1726:102205:23:14:266:343:672:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:θsPG∆XPG(js,Ψ)
33:1727:102219:14:0:280:329:658:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:X(js,Ψ)′θ
33:1728:102228:0:31:343:346:666:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:,
33:1729:102229:31:15:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for a particular supplier with the matchesΨin the data. Note that this measure imposes a cardinal
33:1730:102326:15:15:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(up to scale) interpretation of a supplier’s valuation function, as opposed to identifying a supplier’s
33:1731:102429:15:15:86:525:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:valuation function only up to a positive monotonic transformation. Fox (2010) proves that the cardinal
33:1732:102531:15:15:86:525:590:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:aspects of a related function are identified nonparametrically in a truly finite matching game with
33:1733:102630:15:15:86:126:575:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:transfers.
33:1734:102640:15:15:101:525:560:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Table 2 reports statistics for the distribution of percentage changes in valuation for suppliers. A
33:1735:102739:15:15:86:525:545:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:supplier in the table is a real-life supplier in a particular component category. Only suppliers who
33:1736:102839:15:15:86:525:530:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:sell at least one part to Opel and one car part to another GM brand are affected and so included
33:1737:102935:15:15:86:525:515:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in the table.  The mean loss is tiny, at 0.04%.  The other quantiles are tiny as well.  This partly
33:1738:103034:15:14:86:525:500:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:reflects suppliers where either Opel is a small fraction of car parts or a very large fraction of parts,
33:1739:103138:14:15:86:525:486:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:so GM divesting Opel makes little difference in how specialized the supplier is.  This result also
33:1740:103236:15:15:86:525:471:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:follows from the parameter estimates in Table 1, where the point estimates for the coefficients on
33:1741:103334:15:15:86:525:456:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:brand and especially model specialization are many times larger than the coefficient on parent group
33:1742:103434:15:32:86:155:441:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:specialization.26
33:1743:103451:32:21:86:304:409:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:6.5  International Trade Application
33:1744:103487:21:15:86:525:388:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Appendix D contains estimates of a separate specification motivated by how barriers to international
33:1745:103587:15:37:86:316:373:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:trade may upgrade the quality of domestic suppliers.
33:1746:103639:37:25:86:191:336:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:7  Conclusions
33:1747:103653:25:15:86:525:311:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:This paper discusses the estimation of valuation functions in matching games with transferable utility.
33:1748:103756:15:15:86:525:296:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A matching maximum score estimator is introduced for the matching with trades model of Azevedo
33:1749:103850:15:15:86:525:281:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and Hatfield (2015, Section 6), which has many special cases of empirical relevance. The matching
33:1750:103947:15:15:86:405:266:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:maximum score estimator is computationally simple and semiparametric.
33:1751:104016:15:15:101:525:251:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The empirical work answers two policy questions surrounding the automotive industry. First, the
33:1752:104111:15:15:86:525:236:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:paper estimates the relative loss in valuation to suppliers from decreased specialization from General
33:1753:104213:15:15:86:525:221:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Motors divesting Opel. A forced divestiture ends up hurting most suppliers only a little as the point
33:1754:104314:15:15:86:525:206:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimates to the gains to specialization at model level, which is not affected by the divestment, are
33:1755:104415:15:15:86:525:191:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:higher than the gains to specialization at the parent group level. Second and in an appendix, the paper
33:1756:104518:15:15:86:525:176:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimates the gain to, say, North American suppliers from the presence of Asian-based assemblers in
33:1757:104617:15:15:86:525:161:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:North America. Both estimates are inferred from a new type of data, the portfolios of car part trades
33:1758:104718:15:14:86:169:146:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:from each supplier.
33:1759:104737:14:13:93:525:132:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:26I compute but do not report the small changes in GM’s and Opel’s valuations from divesting Opel. Because the
33:1760:104847:13:9:86:525:119:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:coefficient estimates on assembler specialization in Table 1 are small in magnitude, the overwhelming effect in profit
33:1761:104965:9:0:86:224:110:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:levels is estimated to be on suppliers.
34:1762:105006:0:27:86:158:695:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:A  Proofs
34:1763:105015:27:22:86:337:668:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:A.1  Proposition 1: Rank Order Property
34:1764:105054:22:14:86:525:646:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The proof cites Graham (2011, Theorem 4.1). His theorem is stated for one-to-one, two-sided matching
34:1765:105154:14:15:86:525:632:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:or marriage and, in his notation, considers two observable types of menkandmand two observable
34:1766:105248:15:15:86:525:617:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:types of womenlandn.  Graham’s proof works by considering the so-called suballocation of the
34:1767:105340:15:15:86:525:602:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:two observable types of men and the two observable types of women, the suballocationklmnin his
34:1768:105434:15:15:86:525:587:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:notation. In the suballocationklmn, Graham considers the probability within the suballocation of
34:1769:105530:15:15:86:525:572:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:kandlmatching, which is calledrklmn. The probability ofkmatching withnispklmn−rklmn,
34:1770:105614:15:15:86:525:557:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the probability ofmmatching withlisqklmn−rklmn, and the probability ofmmatching withnis
34:1771:105701:15:15:86:203:542:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f4:1−pklmn−qklmn+rklmn.
34:1772:105721:15:15:101:525:527:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The statement that drawing two matches betweenkandlandmandnare more likely than
34:1773:105800:15:19:86:321:512:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:drawing two matches betweenkandnandmandlis
34:1774:105842:19:8:151:156:493:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
34:1775:105843:8:0:156:270:485:10:g_d0_f8:7:g_d0_f13:1−pklmn−qklmn+rklmn
34:1776:105862:0:8:270:275:493:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
34:1777:105863:8:0:276:311:485:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:rklmn>
34:1778:105869:0:8:314:319:493:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
34:1779:105870:8:0:319:379:485:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f13:pklmn−rklmn

34:1781:105883:8:0:390:450:485:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f13:qklmn−rklmn
34:1782:105894:0:8:451:456:493:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:)
34:1783:105895:8:28:457:525:485:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:.(18)
34:1784:105900:28:15:86:525:457:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Algebra at the end of Section 4.3.2 in Graham, after correcting typos, shows that this inequality is
34:1785:106000:15:15:86:525:442:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:equivalent torklmn> pklmnqklmn. The conclusion of Theorem 4.1 on the same page of Graham can
34:1786:106092:15:15:86:198:427:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:be rewritten to state that
34:1787:106118:15:22:258:525:412:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:δmn+δkl≥δml+δkn(19)
34:1788:106137:22:15:86:525:390:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:if and only ifrklmn> pklmnqklmn, which as just said is equivalent to the inequality (18). The inequality
34:1789:106241:15:15:86:525:375:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(19) can be seen as a matching maximum score inequality (10). Therefore, Graham (2011, Theorem
34:1790:106335:15:15:86:470:360:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:4.1) is a rank order property for one-to-one, two-sided matching without data on prices.
34:1791:106423:15:15:101:525:345:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The setup in the AH model is more general than the model of one-to-one, two-sided matching or
34:1792:106516:15:15:86:525:330:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:marriage in Graham. However, the extra generality can be handled by conditioning. In an matching
34:1793:106612:15:15:86:525:315:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:maximum score inequalityg∈Gin my notation, there are the two observable agent types of buyers
34:1794:106705:15:15:86:525:300:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and the two observable agent types of sellers inHg={b(ω1),s(ω1),b(ω2),s(ω2)}. While the AH
34:1795:106795:15:15:86:525:285:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:model does not necessarily assign roles of buyers and sellers ex ante, a matching maximum score
34:1796:106890:15:15:86:525:270:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:inequality (10) does condition on these roles on the left side of the inequality and the right side of the
34:1797:106996:15:15:86:525:255:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:inequality. A complication is the observable typeb(ω1)that is the buyer onω1on the left side of the
34:1798:107095:15:14:86:525:240:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:inequality could be a seller on, say, tradeω3on the right side of the inequality. This switch of roles
34:1799:107197:14:15:86:336:226:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of buyer and seller does not change the proof in Graham.
34:1800:107253:15:15:101:526:211:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Likewise, agents in the AH model make sets of trades(Φ,Ψ). This can be handled by conditioning
34:1801:107347:15:15:86:525:196:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:on the set of trades(Φj,Ψj)other thanω1–ω4for all four observable agent types inj∈Hg. In other
34:1802:107441:15:0:86:344:181:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:words, condition on the joint eventCthatb(ω1)picks either

35:1916:110514:15:15:86:525:147:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:same objective function value or a lower objective function value where some smaller weight contributes

35:1918:110713:15:0:86:341:117:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:uniquely) globally maximized at the true parameter value.
36:1919:110772:0:25:86:525:695:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:B  Estimation and Inference for the Car Parts Empirical Work
36:1920:110832:25:15:86:525:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I first describe point estimation and then inference. I sample 10,000 inequalities for each of 29 matching
36:1921:110938:15:15:86:525:655:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:markets given by component categories. For the 30th component category, I use the maximum number
36:1922:111034:15:15:86:525:640:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of inequalities, 8,272, for that market. To create one of the 10,000 inequalities for a market, I randomly
36:1923:111140:15:14:86:525:625:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:sample two car parts from different suppliers and include the resulting matching maximum score
36:1924:111234:14:15:86:401:611:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:inequality where the two car parts are exchanged between the suppliers.
36:1925:111305:15:15:101:525:596:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I use the numerical optimization routine differential evolution, in Mathematica. For differential
36:1926:111402:15:15:86:525:581:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:evolution, I use a population of 250 points and a maximum of 15,000 iterations.  The numerical
36:1927:111496:15:15:86:525:566:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:optimization is run 20 times with different initial populations of 250 points. For the specification in
36:1928:111599:15:15:86:525:551:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Table 1, all 20 runs found the same objective function value and the same point estimates, up to two
36:1929:111699:15:15:86:160:536:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:significant digits.
36:1930:111718:15:15:101:525:521:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:In the maximum score objective function, an inequality is satisfied if the left side plus the constant
36:1931:111820:15:15:86:525:506:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:+0.0000000001 exceeds the right side.  This small perturbation to the sum of profits on the left
36:1932:111916:15:15:86:525:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:side ensures that inequalities such as0>0are counted as being satisfied consistently, rather than
36:1933:112013:15:15:86:525:476:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f11:inconsistently because of some numerical-approximation error resulting in, say,2.0×10−15>1.0×
36:1934:112106:15:15:86:114:461:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f4:10−15.
36:1935:112112:15:15:101:525:446:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I use the inference procedure of Romano and Shaikh (2008), which is valid under both set identifi-
36:1936:112210:15:15:86:525:431:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:cation and point identification. LetΘ0be the identified set for the parameterθ. The authors provide
36:1937:112309:15:15:86:525:416:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a subsampling procedure to construct a confidence regionCcalled, by those authors, a “confidence
36:1938:112405:15:15:86:525:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:region for the identifiable parameters that is uniformly consistent in level”, under the conditions of
36:1939:112507:15:15:86:525:386:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:their Theorem 3.3. This definition of the properties of a confidence region is equation (3) of their
36:1940:112607:15:14:86:525:371:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:paper. Under easier to verify conditions, their procedure produces “confidence regions for identifiable
36:1941:112710:14:15:86:525:357:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:parameters that are pointwise consistent in level”, or their equation (2). Computationally, I implement
36:1942:112813:15:15:86:255:342:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:equations (12) and (10) in their paper.
36:1943:112852:15:15:101:525:327:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I have 30 component categories. I treat these component categories as separate markets for the
36:1944:112946:15:15:86:525:312:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:industry-specific reasons discussed in the main text. I perform asymptotics in the number of suppliers
36:1945:113048:15:15:86:525:297:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in the market, as this is an explicitly two-sided market where a supplier cannot also be an assembler,
36:1946:113150:15:15:86:525:282:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:as in Example 2. Subsampling requires a choice of subsample size. Unfortunately, the literature has
36:1947:113249:15:15:86:525:267:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:not provided a data driven method to pick this tuning parameter. I use 33% of the suppliers from
36:1948:113345:15:15:86:525:252:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:each of the 30 component categories. Given each subsampled set of suppliers, that subsample uses
36:1949:113441:15:15:86:525:237:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:only matching maximum score inequalities where both suppliers whose valuation functions are in the
36:1950:113539:15:15:86:525:222:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:inequality are in the subsample. I use 500 subsamples; in experiments results are robust when using
36:1951:113638:15:15:86:163:207:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:more subsamples.
36:1952:113654:15:15:101:525:192:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:In the car parts empirical work, the maximum score or maximum rank correlation objective func-
36:1953:113748:15:35:86:265:177:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tion is, forD= 30component categories,
36:1954:113786:35:0:182:215:142:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:Q(θ) =
36:1955:113792:0:10:218:226:159:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:(
36:1956:113793:10:15:231:239:149:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:N
36:1957:113794:15:0:233:238:134:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:2
36:1958:113795:0:7:245:276:159:10:g_d0_f16:7:g_d0_f13:)−1D
36:1959:113799:7:22:265:279:152:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:∑
36:1960:113800:22:0:265:279:130:7:g_d0_f13:7:g_d0_f9:d=1
36:1961:113803:0:24:281:298:155:7:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f16:Nd−1∑
36:1962:113808:24:0:283:300:131:7:g_d0_f13:7:g_d0_f9:i1=1
36:1963:113812:0:24:313:325:155:7:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f16:Nd∑
36:1964:113815:24:0:304:333:131:7:g_d0_f13:7:g_d0_f9:i2=i1+1
36:1965:113822:0:23:343:357:152:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:∑
36:1966:113823:23:0:335:365:129:7:g_d0_f13:5:g_d0_f17:g∈Gdi1,i2
36:1967:113832:0:0:368:373:142:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:1
36:1968:113833:0:8:375:379:150:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:[
36:1969:113834:8:0:379:420:142:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f8:Z′g,dθ≥0
36:1970:113842:0:8:420:424:150:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:]
36:1971:113843:8:39:426:429:142:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:,
36:1972:113844:39:15:86:525:103:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:whereGdi1,i2is the set of included matching maximum score inequalities wherei1andi2exchange one
36:1973:113939:15:0:86:525:88:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:car part each. Romano and Shaikh (2008) is written where one minimizes a function and where the
37:1974:114036:0:15:86:525:695:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:population objective function’s minimum value is 0. In maximum score, one maximizes the objective
37:1975:114133:15:15:86:525:680:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:function value and the value of the population objective function can only be estimated using the
37:1976:114230:15:15:86:525:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:finite sample objective function. Following the suggestion at the beginning of their Section 3.2, I work
37:1977:114334:15:15:86:316:650:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:with the objective function−Q(θ)−(−maxθQ(θ)).
37:1978:114379:15:15:101:525:635:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:I define the “sample size” for the entire procedure to beN= maxd∈DNd. This choice is arbitrary
37:1979:114473:15:15:86:525:620:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and does not impact the reported confidence regions.  I implement the procedure of Romano and
37:1980:114566:15:0:86:400:605:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Shaikh (2008) using the rate of convergence for the objective function of
37:1981:114639:0:9:403:411:614:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:√
37:1982:114640:9:14:412:525:605:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:N, following the results of
37:1983:114667:14:15:86:460:591:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Sherman (1993) for the case of point identified maximum rank correlation estimators.
37:1984:114751:15:15:101:525:576:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The confidence regions reported in tables are projections onto the axes of the confidence region
37:1985:114847:15:15:86:525:561:10:g_d0_f27:10:g_d0_f4:Cfrom Romano and Shaikh (2008). Computationally, the lower bound for the confidence region for
37:1986:114941:15:15:86:525:546:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a scalar parameterθ1is found by minimizing the parameterθ1subject to the constraint that the
37:1987:115033:15:15:86:525:531:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:entire parameter vectorθis inC. Likewise, the upper bound for the confidence regionθ1is found by
37:1988:115129:15:38:86:436:516:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:maximizing the parameterθ1subject to the entire parameter vector being inC.
37:1989:115204:38:24:86:525:478:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C  Alternative Weighting Schemes for Specialization Measures
37:1990:115264:24:15:86:525:454:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:This appendix discusses versions of the estimates in Table 1 where the included HHI specialization
37:1991:115362:15:15:86:525:439:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:measures use different weighting schemes, many involving data on car sales for car models in Europe
37:1992:115461:15:15:86:525:424:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and the United States. These alternative weighting schemes result in worse statistical fit than the

37:1994:115663:15:15:86:312:394:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:estimates in this appendix instead of the main text.
37:1995:115715:15:15:101:525:379:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:In terms of sales, car models primarily sold in Europe are matched to European sales from Western
37:1996:115812:15:15:86:525:364:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Europe and car models primarily from North America are matched to sales from the United States.
